He who compiled this book said when he completed for you, O people, this book which is a part of the science of medicine in its entirety and reached the goal in it from its clarity and explanation, I saw that I complete it for you with this article which is a part of the work by hand.
Because work by hand is refined in our country and in our time completely absent, so that it was almost about to be studied and its trace would be cut off. And what remained of it were simple drawings in the books of the ancients which my hands corrected and made their errors and confusion clear until I clarified its meanings and distanced its benefit.
So I saw that I revive it and compile in it this article on the path of explanation, clarity, and brevity and bring forth images of instruments,  and all tools of work because it is from increase of explanation and help of what is needed for it.
And the reason why there is no skilled craftsman by hand in our time is because the craft of medicine is long and it befits its owner to study before that the science of anatomy which Galen described. Until he stands on the benefits of the organs and their systems and temperaments, their connection and separation, and the knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their number, their exits, veins, arteries, and the places of their exits.
And therefore Hippocrates said that physicians by name are many and by deed few, especially in the craft of the hand, and we have mentioned from that a part in the introduction to this book.
Because he who is not learned in what we have mentioned from anatomy has not escaped falling into an error that kills people by it, as I have seen many times who imagined themselves in this science and claimed it without knowledge or study.
And that because I saw a physician ignorant who cut on a tumor of a swine in the neck of a woman, so he severed some arteries of the neck, and she bled until she fell dead before his eyes.
I saw another physician who advanced in removing a calculus from a man who had been wounded in the bladder, and the calculus was large so he was afraid, and he removed it with a piece of the urinary bladder's membrane. And the man died after about three days, and I was summoned to remove it, and I saw from the size of the calculus and the state of the sick man that I estimated his condition accordingly.
And I saw another physician who was making a living with some leaders of our country on medicine.
So it happened to a black boy who had a fracture in his leg near the heel with a wound, and the physician, out of ignorance, hastened and tightened the fracture on the wound with splints and bandages tightly, leaving no room for the wound to breathe.
Then he left him on his whims and abandoned him for days, ordering him not to remove the bandage until his leg and foot swelled, and he was headed towards death.
So I was summoned to him and hastened to remove the bandage, and he found relief and escaped from his pain except that the corruption had become strong in the limb, and I was unable to reverse it.
And the corruption continued to spread in the limb until he died.
And I saw another physician who treated a cancerous tumor, and it became worse after days until the suffering of his patient increased greatly because if cancer is from black humors, it should not be exposed to iron at all.
Unless it is in a limb that can be completely removed.
And for this reason, my sons, it is necessary for you to learn that the work with the hand is divided into two parts: work accompanied by safety and work that brings harm in most cases.
And I have warned in every place where this book is reached about the work that involves danger and fear, so it is necessary for you to avoid it and reject it.
So that the ignorant may not find a way to speak and revile, take for yourselves firmness and caution, and satisfy yourselves with gentleness and steadfastness.
And use the best way that leads to safety and a good outcome, and beware of dangerous and difficult diseases.
And guard yourselves from what you fear might enter upon you of doubt in your religion and worldly affairs, for it is more lasting for your own sake, and higher in this world and the next for your destinies.
For Galen said in some of his instructions: "Do not treat a bad disease so that you are called bad physicians."
And this treatise has been divided into three chapters.
The First Chapter.
On cauterization with fire and cauterization with a sharp drug, described systematically from the century to the present, and pictures of instruments and cautery tools, and everything needed in manual work.
The Second Chapter.
On incision, evacuation, bloodletting, cupping, and surgery, including the extraction of arrows and the like, all described systematically and arranged, with pictures of instruments.
The Third Chapter.
On setting bones, dislocations, and treatment of fractures and the like, described systematically and arranged from the century to the present, with pictures of instruments.
The First Chapter.
On Cauterization.
And before we mention how to work with it, it is necessary to mention the way of its benefits and harms, and in what temperament it is used.
And I say that the talk on how to benefit from cauterization and its harms is a long discussion, a precise science, and a hidden secret, and many of the wise have spoken about it.
And they differed about it, and I have abbreviated from their words as much as possible for fear of prolixity.
I say that the purging is beneficial in general for every bad constitution that exists with a substance and without a substance, except for two constitutions: the hot constitution without a substance and the dry constitution without a substance.
As for the dry constitution with a substance, there has been disagreement about it. Some have said that purging is beneficial in it, while others have said the opposite, that purging is not suitable for a disease that is from heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
And it is impossible to cure a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry medicine, and he who says the opposite said that purging by fire can be beneficial for a hot and dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. Because when you add the body of a human being and its moisture to the nature of fire, you make the body of the human being cold.
And I say what he says because experience has revealed that to me many times, unless it is not supposed by one who has practiced and traveled in the field of purging to a great extent. And stood on the difference of people's constitutions and the conditions of diseases in themselves, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
As for the rest of the constitutions, there is no fear for you from them, especially the cold and wet diseases, because all physicians have agreed on it and have not disagreed on the benefit of purging in them.
And know, my sons, that the secret of healing is purging by fire and its preference over purging by burning medicine because fire is a single essence whose action does not exceed the member that is cauterized and does not harm another connected member except for slight harm.
And purging by burning medicine may exceed its action to what is beyond the members and may cause a disease in the member that is difficult to treat and may even kill, and fire because of its honor and generosity of essence does not do that except if it is excessive.
And this has become clear to us by experience through the length of service and care for the craft and standing upon the realities of the matter.
For this reason, I have dispensed with lengthy discourse, although if it were fitting for this book of mine, I would have presented to you in fire a secret and hidden manner and the way of doing it in bodies and removing it from diseases by philosophical and demonstrative speech that would strike your understanding.
And know, O sons, that they have differed concerning the time which is suitable for cauterization and have made the best time to be the time of spring.
And I say that cauterization can be suitable in every time because the harm caused by time is overshadowed by the benefit brought about by cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is from a necessary and strong pain, a menacing one that cannot tolerate delay because of what might follow it, which would be a harm greater than the slight damage caused by time.
And do not put in your mind, O sons, what the common people and physicians imagine that cauterization which cures a disease will never return again and make it final.
And it is not fitting for you to think that cauterization is like a medicine that corrects the humors and dries up the humors which are the cause of pain.
Except that cauterization is preferable to medicine in the speed of its success, strength of its effect, and intensity of its power.
And the disease may return after a time, depending on the patient's temperament, the strength of his illness, and what is prepared in his body from the gathering of humors within him and his negligence in acquiring them from food and so on from such causes.
God willing, except that the disease in which cauterization is used would be a mild one and in an organ with little humors and dampness. Like the pain of a molar and its likes, it is possible that there will be no return of that pain, and this occurs at the least.
And as for the saying of the common people, that when a wound occurs its treatment is finished, it is a correct statement contrary to what they think because they believe that there is no remedy that will benefit after the occurrence of a wound, and the matter is otherwise.
And the meaning of that which is said that "the wound" is the last of treatments is that when we used types of treatment for a disease from among diseases, and those medicines did not benefit, and then we used another thing that was a wound, then it benefited; therefore, it happened that "the wound" is the last of treatments. Not on the meaning to which the common people and many ignorant physicians went.
And those before mentioned said that a wound with gold is better than a wound with iron, and they said that because of the moderation of gold and its noble nature, and they said that it does not cause cauterization of the place of the wound, and that is not at all true.
Because I have tried it, and found that it does that in some bodies but not others, and the wound with it is better and more excellent than iron as they said, except that if you heat the gold plate in the fire, it will not become clear to you when it heats to the degree you want for the redness of gold.
And because it quickly becomes cold, and if you increase it in heat, it melts in the fire, and if you break it, then the craftsman is ruined by that in his work, therefore, the wound with iron has become faster and more correct for us in action, God willing.
And I have arranged this chapter on wounds into sections that I have organized from the head to the foot so that it is easy for the student what he wants from it, God willing.
The First Section.
In wounds of the head, one kind.
This application is beneficial from the excess of humidity and coldness on the brain, which are the cause of headache and much discharge from the head towards the eyes and ears, and much sleep and toothache and sore throat. And in general for every disease that appears from coldness like stroke, epilepsy, and muteness and similar diseases.
The picture of this application is that you order the sick person first to vomit with the purgative medicine for the head three nights or four, according to what the strength of the sick person and his nature and habit require.
Then you order him to shave his head with the razor, then sit him in front of you seated with his hands on his chest.
Then you put the root of your hand on the root of his nose between his eyes, and where your middle finger ends, mark that place with the lead.
Then warm the olive-green iron whose picture is this.
When a part of the skull has been exposed like the size of an almond or a lentil, raise your hand, otherwise, re-apply your hand with the same iron or another if it cools. Until you see what I told you from the bone, then take some salt and dissolve it in water and soak a piece of cotton wool in it and place it on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then carry upon it cotton wool soaked in ghee and leave it on until the char has gone from the fire, then treat him with the four ointment until he heals if God wills.
And they have said that the wound as long as it remains open extends the pus, so it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have mentioned that the skin should be cauterized to the bone and hold the iron until some thickness of the bone burns, then after that what has burned from the bone is removed, then treated.
Others say that one should exaggerate the cauterization until it affects the bone strongly, so that it falls away from the bone like a small gemstone or star, and they claimed that it exhales fumes from the head and leaves the wound open for a long time.
Then he treats until it heals, and I do not see these two types of cauterization at all except in some people and on the path of conjecture. Leaving it with me is better, and safe, if it is, because the head swells when its natural connection is separated, as we have seen in other organs.
Especially when the patient's head is naturally weak, and the first type of cauterization is safer and better for me, and with it I act, and do it safely, God willing.
The Second Chapter.
In the head also.
If there is a chronic headache that has lasted for the patient and he used poultices, cauteries, compresses, ointments and bandages, and especially if he had been cauterized with the single cauterization we described and nothing of that helped him, then look. Then if the patient's head is strong in its structure by nature and was not weak, and he found a severe coldness, cauterize with another cauterization slightly above that one. Then cauterize on each horn of his head until the thickness of the skin goes and the bone is exposed to the degree we described. And cauterize on the back of his head in the place known as the axe, and lighten your hand in this one and do not expose the bone because the patient finds great pain from it unlike the pain of all other cauterizations of the head, and I will mention this cauterization in its place.
The cautery that is used to cauterize the horns of the head and its back should be gentler than the one used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is its shape.
Chapter Three.
Concerning the unprotracted headache.
If headache occurs in the fissure of the head with a pounding pain and the pain extends to the eye, empty the patient with purgatives for the head and use all the treatment mentioned in the classifications of diseases. If this does not work, then treat it on two faces. Either with a sharp, burning medicine or with iron.
As for treatment with a burning medicine, take one clove of garlic, peel it and cut off its ends on both sides, then split the location of the pain in the temple with a wide scalpel until there is a place under the skin that can accommodate the clove.
Insert it under the skin until it disappears, then pull on it with forceps in a tight grip and leave it for about fifteen hours, then remove it and take out the garlic and leave the wound for two or three days, then carry on.
Cover it with cotton soaked in butter until the place is greasy, then treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing. And if you wish, do this with some of the burning medicines that I gave you in article eighteen on burning medicines.
As for treatment with iron, it is like this: heat the iron whose picture is shown here.
And it is called the nail-shaped iron because its head resembles a nail with some engraving and in its center, a small protrusion.
Then place it on the location of the pain and hold your hand while you turn the iron slightly, and the amount that burns from the thickness of the skin should be like half of it. And raise your hand so that you do not burn the artery below which causes bleeding, then absorb cotton in salt water and place it on the location and leave it for three days. Then carry the cotton with butter and treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, cut this fistula with the instrument born from the steel and preserve it from severing the artery in this unchronic fistula particularly.
Chapter Four.
On chronic fistulas.
If you have treated the fistula with what we mentioned of the aforementioned treatment and what we mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment did not work, and you saw from the cause what does not respond to what we mentioned from the first kind by medicine or the second kind by fire. Then it is necessary to heat the steel instrument until it whitens after you have learned on the place of pain with a line equal in length to half a finger or thereabouts, and leave your hand once while you tighten it until you cut the artery and reach near the bone.
Except that it is necessary for you to beware of the jawbone which moves when chewing, so it burns the muscle or the nerve that moves it, and causes tension.
And be careful and vigilant from the bleeding of the artery you cut for there is danger in cutting it. Especially for one who does not know what to do and has no experience, leaving the work is preferable.
And it will come to mention the treatment of the bleeding that occurs from the artery in its place in this book, God willing, if you see from the cause what this kind of cauterization does not do.
And if you see the body of the sick person  likely to be cauterized in the middle of the head as we described and treated the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you wish, use the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter of searing the artery with a double-edged blade, for it is a better and more effective cautery than this.
Chapter Five.
On cauterizing ear pains.
If pain occurs in the ear due to cold, it is treated with laxatives and all the treatments mentioned in the division. And if the pain does not go away, apply the plate called "al-naqtah" whose image is this.
Then it is placed on it after heating it around the whole ear as it revolves, or around both of them if the pain is in both. And it is removed by the cautery a little from the base of the ear after learning its position with lead, and the cautery should be the size of ten points in each ear or thereabouts. Then the places are treated until they heal, God willing.
The Sixth Chapter.
On the Power of the Cautery.
The cautery that is treated with cauterization is one of the types that arise from phlegm as mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
And it avoids the cautery that arises from phlegm and hardening of nerves.
When this type of cautery is treated with poultices, compresses, and gargles and your treatment was not effective, then it is necessary that the diseased area be cauterized with three cauterizations. One at the base of the ear and the second slightly below its crest, and the third at the meeting of the lips.
And make your cautery from the opposite side of the diseased side because relaxation occurs in the side that appears healthy.
And the image of the cautery is that you make it with a cauterization opposite the top of the ear under the corner of the head slightly, and another in the crest, and its length should be the length of the thumb.
Lower the cautery with your hand until it burns about half the thickness of the skin, and this is the image of the cauterization plate, which is a type of knife whose image has been shown to you, but it is slightly gentler than that, as you see. The blade should be slightly thick and then the place is treated with what has been mentioned before until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Seven.
On Chronic Stroke.
If the stroke persists and you have treated it with what has been mentioned, and your treatment did not work, and there is no fever in the patient, then give him four doses of  the drug One dose on each horn of his head and one dose in the middle of the head as we have mentioned, and one dose at the back of the head as previously mentioned.
The recipe for the cauterization as previously mentioned, and it may also be cauterized with one dose on the mouth of the stomach to be more effective, then treated as before.
Chapter Eight.
On Forgetfulness.
He who has forgetfulness from phlegm should first be given the patient large quantities of purging drinks and purified pills for the brain.
Then his head is shaved completely and a mustard poultice as written in the article on the plasters is applied to the back of his head several times because it is a kind of cauterization.
And do it on the same order that was mentioned there, if he is healed by this, otherwise give him three doses at the back of his head arranged from the top of the head to the base of the neck.
And make between each dose and the next a thickness of a finger, then treat the cauterization as before, if you want to increase it and the patient is capable of it, give him the middle dose.
And if you want to increase it, then give him doses on the horns, then treat him until he is healed, and the cauterization should be olive oil as previously mentioned.
Chapter Nine.
On Paralysis and Relaxation of the Whole Body.
It is necessary that you proceed in purifying the head with the implements and what we have mentioned then shave the patient's head, then make a incision in the middle of the head and an incision on each horn of the head and an incision on its back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck, if it is necessary in a case of relaxation of the body to more than that and the patient was likely for that and the disease is strong and severe then make four incisions on the vertebrae of his back. And make the incision until it burns from the skin most of it and raise your hand then treat him as has been mentioned before until he heals if God wills, and be the cauterizing instrument olive-like.
The tenth chapter.
On how to treat epilepsy.
Only the epileptic who is afflicted with epilepsy from phlegm should be cauterized, so it is necessary that his nose be cleansed first with the large implements and all the treatment that we have mentioned in the division if the patient is large and likely to take the medicine.
But if he is a child who cannot tolerate medicine, then let him use gargles and cleansing mouthwashes for the brain before that for many days with improvement of his nutrition.
Then shave his head and then make one incision in the middle of the head as has been mentioned before, and another incision at its back. And on each horn of his head, an incision; if the patient is strong and likely, then make the incisions that were mentioned for paralysis and relaxation of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and back, and be the cauterizing instrument olive-like as in the description that has come before.
If the patient is a child, then make the cautery gentle in this form.
The eleventh chapter.
On how to treat intestinal worms.
If the cause of melancholia is putrid moisture and thick phlegm, use the cauteries mentioned in the chapter on apoplexy.
If the cause of melancholia is a black, viscous humor and the body of the sick person is moist and corrupt, purify his nose as mentioned before in the division.
Then shave the head of the sick person and then make a tight cake of cotton like a circle and put it in the middle of his head, and the sick person is sitting upright holding from each side, and take one cupful of old sheep fat.
Then heat it on the fire at a moderate heat as much as the finger can bear if it is inserted in it, then empty it in the middle of his head in the circle and leave it until it cools, do this to the sick person every week once with all his good treatment until he heals, if Allah wills.
And if you wish, cauterize it with small, many drops without holding your hand to the cautery, but make it a smearing, for this type of cautery moistens the brain moderately.
Then apply cotton soaked in fat or chicken tallow on top of it.
Chapter the Twelfth.
In cauterizing water coming down from the eye.
If it becomes apparent to you the beginning of water coming down from the eye with the signs mentioned in the division, then hasten to purify the head of the sick person and protect him from all moisture and make him sweat in the bath on an empty stomach for days.
Then once, shave his head and cauterize in the middle of the head, then cauterize two cauterizations on the temples if the beginning of the eye water coming down is from both eyes, or from one side if it is from one eye.
Then cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries under the skin, let the cauterizations be long in width on the temples and take care not to bleed.
If you see something of it, cut it where it is with any treatment that you can manage and I will come to the wisdom in the matter of severing the veins and cutting them and guarding against bleeding.
And it may be seared in the nape of the neck under two bones, smooth ones.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
On Chronic Flowing of Tears.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and constant, and they come from the veins and arteries in the outside of the head, and you are certain that this is from a cold and large phlegm, boil the cautery which I have described at the beginning of the flowing water. Boil a cautery in the middle of the head and two on the temples, and two at the nape of the neck under the bones. And if you need to increase it, boil a cautery on each side from the angle of the eye to the edge of the eyebrow with a small soldering iron.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing a Nostrils Malodour.
If you treated it with what we have mentioned in the section and the treatment did not benefit, then immediately make the patient put on qinqiya three nights, then shave his head and cauterize the middle of the head with the olive soldering iron. Then cauterize with the nail soldering iron two above the eyebrows under the hair slightly, and guard against the artery, do not cut it. And this is a picture of the nail soldering iron.
The Fifteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Relaxation of the Eyelid.
If the eyelid has relaxed because of a disease or moisture, cauterize the eyelid with one cautery using this crescent soldering iron.
And if you wish, cauterize slightly above the eyebrows, two on each side, and be spaced from the temples, and let the length of each cautery be along the eyebrow.
Do not extend your hand in cautery beyond what burns a third of the skin, and the appearance of the cautery should be like this.
The Sixteenth Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Eyelid.
If its borders turn inward and the eye is sunken, then cautery in it is of two kinds. Either cautery by fire or cautery by a burning drug, as for cauterizing it by fire, order the patient before that to leave its borders if he is one whose they are inflamed until they grow long and equal.
If it is cauterized at its growth, then tie his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until it grows, and if it has grown and become equal, place the patient's head in your stone block, then teach on the eyelid of the eye with lead pencil a sign in the shape of an As leaf.
And the beginning of the mark is near the borders, then you place under the eyelid cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of the quince, and heat the cautery with this image.
Then cauterize on the shape which you have taught little by little in many times until the surface of the skin burns, which is like the shape of the As leaf altogether, a special appearance and a sign of the health of your work that you see the eyelid has become tanned and the hair has risen above the fleshy lining of the eye.
Then raise your hand at that time and leave him three days, then carry on it cotton with butter until the scabs are shed, then treat him with ointment until he heals, if God wills, if something of the hair returns after a while and the eyelid relaxes.
Then repeat the cautery on that place as you did first, if the hair is in the lower eyelid, hold it until it returns to its natural place and do not remove the hair from the eye, as for cauterizing with a burning drug, order the patient to leave the borders until they grow long and equal.
Then you make a sheet of paper, and take from the usual soap and unquenched lime, one drachm or so of each, then grind them both well together and do this quickly lest they dry. Then you spread it on the paper you made in the shape of a leaf of as, and put it on one or both eyelids and place under the eye cotton soaked in egg white and the patient's head in your stone.
And you place your index finger above the medicine and press it lightly and move it whenever the patient feels the sting of the medicine because he will feel a sensation like fire, as long as he feels the sting, leave the medicine and move it with your finger, if the sting stops, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has risen as it does when you smell fire or cut, otherwise, repeat on it of the medicine on the place which was not affected by the medicine and did not turn black until you complete your work and the eye is inflamed then put cotton on it with butter until the sting of burning subsides.
Then treat it with palm ointment or another until it heals, and it is necessary for you when working that you exercise extreme caution that nothing of the medicine falls into the eye, if the eyelid relaxes after days and we fear something in the hair entering the eye.
Then repeat the medicine on that place of the eyelid which relaxed especially as you did at first, then treat it until it heals, and this is a picture of a leaf of as.
And know that people's eyes differ in size and smallness, so according to that, let your inflaming be, and it is not a hidden path of right for one who has experience in this craft.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
In the kind of ulcer which appears in the corner of the eye.
If you have treated the ulcers as mentioned in the classifications of diseases and your treatment has been ineffective, then it is necessary to cauterize them with this method.
Command the patient to place his head in a block and have an attendant hold his head between your hands, holding it so that it does not move or strike against anything.
Then, place cotton moistened in egg white or the saliva of the black fig on his eyes, and then heat the cautery whose image is depicted here.
It should be hollow like the tube of an eagle's feather from one end which is for cauterization, and if you wish, the other end can be open, and if you wish it can be solid like a probe; however, this hollow one is better for your work, God willing.
Then, if it is open, squeeze the ulcer and remove the pus from it, or dry it out; and if it is not open, then open it and extract the pus, and then place the cautery on top of it while it is very hot, holding it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
And keep your hand a little distance from the eye, towards the nose when cauterizing so that your hand does not slip or make the patient nervous causing the cautery to fall into the eyelid and spoil it; if in the first cauterization it reaches the bone, otherwise, reheat the cautery again if needed.
Leave him for three days, then apply cotton soaked in butter to it and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals; if it has gone forty days and has not healed, apply the sharp medicinal powder until the bone is exposed and follow what will be mentioned about it in its chapter, God willing.
And another method of cauterizing ulcers, mentioned by some earlier physicians, is to aim at the location of the ulcer, make a cut there, and place a fine probe in the same incision, whose image is depicted here.
Pour into it a measure the weight of a drachma of melted lead and hold your hand firmly on the beak, pressing well so that the patient does not move at all, lest the molten lead flow into his eye. And it is necessary to place on the eye of the patient a cotton swab moistened in albumen or in water.
For lead burns the place of the nasal polyp and cleanses it with a wondrous cure, if the polyp is cleansed by what has been mentioned of cauterization and treatment, otherwise there is no choice but to use the nostril puncture and return the polyp to the nostril's passage as will be mentioned in its specific place.
Chapter Eighteen.
In cauterizing a cleft lip.
A cleft in the lip, called a harelip, occurs frequently, especially in boys' lips; it happens often. If this cleft is treated with what has been mentioned in the section and the treatment did not work, then take a small, knife-like iron to cauterize like this...
Its hollow is like the blade of a knife, then you place it firmly into the same cleft until the cauterization reaches the depth of the cleft and then treat it with honey until it heals God willing.
Chapter Nineteen.
In cauterizing a polyp that occurs in the mouth.
If it appears at the root of the gums, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, as a swelling then bursts and becomes a flowing pus polyp.  And you treat it and it did not benefit from treatment, then it is necessary to heat an iron cautery in a measure that fits the polyp...
... then you insert it firmly into the polyp's hole and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its entire depth, doing this once or twice then treat it afterward with what has been mentioned of treatment until it heals God willing.
If the substance is severed and healed, otherwise it is necessary to examine the place and remove the decayed bone according to what will come in its chapter, if God wills.
The twentieth chapter.
Of loose and relaxed gums.
If the gums have become loose because of moisture and the teeth have moved, and you have treated them with medications but they did not benefit, then place the head of the patient in a stone mortar, then heat the iron instrument whose image comes after this, after placing the tube on the tooth.
And insert the iron instrument into it with a handle of quicklime, and hold your hand slightly until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth, then raise your hand and repeat the iron instrument several times according to what you desire, then the patient fills his mouth with salt water.
And he holds it for an hour and spits it out, then the loose tooth will be fixed, the relaxed gums will tighten, and the rotten moisture will dry up.
The twenty-first chapter.
Of toothache.
If the toothache is from cold or there is a worm in it, and the treatment with medications did not benefit, then its treatment is in two ways: either treatment with butter or treatment with fire.
As for treatment with butter, take the cow butter and boil it in an iron ladle or a bowl, then take cotton, wind it on the end of a stick, dip it in the boiling butter, and put it on the aching tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools.
Then repeat it several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth, and if you want, dip a bandage or cotton in cold butter and put it on the aching tooth and place the heated iron above it until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterizing it with fire, you should resort to a copper or iron pipe with some thickness in its body so that the heat of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient. Then, take the heated iron and place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the iron cools. Do this several times.
If the pain goes away on that same day or another, it is necessary after cauterizing to fill the patient's mouth with good fat and keep it for an hour then spit it out. This is the picture of the cauterizing iron.
You cauterize with any side you wish and on the count that you can, and this is the picture of the pipe.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
Cauterizing Pigs.
If the pigs are due to phlegm and cold humors and they do not respond to ripening with medicine, and you want rapid ripening, then heat the hollow iron cauterizing instrument whose picture is shown, open at both ends.
So that the smoke comes out from the other end when cauterizing, place it covered on the same tumor once and a second time if you need to until you reach the depth of the tumor. If the tumor is small, make the cauterizing iron equal to the size of the tumor.
Then leave it for three days and apply cotton soaked in butter on top of it until what was burned by the fire goes away, then treat it with ointment and cauterizing until it heals God willing.
The Twenty-Third Chapter.
Cauterizing from Hoarseness of Voice and Shortness of Breath.
If the phlegm has overwhelmed the windpipe, especially if this is accompanied by a cold temperament, it is necessary for the patient to first evacuate with laxative medicines, then cauterize in the notch of the chest at the root of the larynx in the lower position.
Beware that you do not reach the pharynx with the cauterizing iron and burn from the skin except half of it, then cauterize again at the juncture of the neck at the end of its last pearl with a burning point and make the cautery as described before.
Then treat it with what has been mentioned before until it heals, God willing.
The Twenty-Fourth Chapter.
In cauterizing ailments of the lungs and cough.
If the cough and lung disease is from cold humors and there is no fever or plague, and the illness is chronic, cauterize two irons above the collarbones in the low, soft, empty places and another iron in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
And make the cautery nail-shaped as described before, and if you wish, let your cauterizing iron be a point, with the cautery called "the point," whose image has been described previously in the section on cauterizing earaches, and let it be thirty points or so.
Then treat him with what has been mentioned before until it heals, and you can make a cautery with three branches in this form, and hasten the cauterization with it because you cauterize with it three cauterizations in one time, and this is the image of the cautery.
The Twenty-Fifth Chapter.
In cauterizing the armpit.
If the head of the humerus has become dislocated due to slippery humors or it did not set properly when returned after being dislocated, so that it becomes a habit to return then become dislocated at the slightest movement as we have seen, then it is necessary to return the jaw first. Then, the patient lies on his back or right side, and you raise the skin inside the armpit upward with your left hand fingers if the joint has dislocated inward.
Then comes the heated cauterizing iron with two points, the picture of which is shown here.
Then, with it, the skin is cauterized until it penetrates to the other side, and the shape of the cautery comes out as four cauterizations.  It may also be cauterized with a cauterizing iron having three points, in which case the shape of the cautery will then be six cauterizations, and the points are on the back of the instrument.
And this is the picture of the cauterizing iron with three points.
And one may be added to this number, so that the cauterizations become eight. Then, the cauterized instrument with a crushed salt-bearing mortar is applied on top of it, and then the patient is put to rest, and the limb is not moved for a while until it strengthens, although dislocation upward rarely happens.
So it is cauterized over the shoulder joint with one well-made cautery incision or many cauterizations in drops, because the articulation hardens, moisture goes away, and the wound heals.
The Sixth Twenty Chapter.
On Cauterizing the Stomach.
If, in the stomach, there is cold and a great deal of moisture until it is expelled from its nature and phlegm has increased to it, and it was treated with various treatments but it did not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient lies on his back and extends his legs and arms, then three cauterizations are made. One cauterization under the chest spoon-full, as much as a finger, with a well-made cautery instrument, and two cauterizations below on both sides of the single cautery until the shape of the cauterizations becomes triangular, and they are kept apart so that they do not meet if they should merge. And the depth of the cautery is one-third the thickness of the skin, and this is the shape of the cauterizations.
On this picture and to this extent no more.
If you wish, you may cauterize it like one large spot in the middle of the stomach, in this way.
And the cautery iron with which you cauterize this single spot should be circular, in this way.
And the stomach may be cauterized in spots for one who has been injured from this cautery, which is to learn on the stomach dots on the extent that you desire with the stylus, then cauterize it with a pointed cautery iron, then treat it with the treatment that I present until it heals.
The Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
In cauterizing a cold liver.
If it is presented from the liver pain about coldness and moisture or about a boiling wind until it has gone out of its natural temperament excessively, and the sick person was treated with what we mentioned in the division, and that did not benefit him. Then it becomes necessary that the sick person lie on his side and with the stylus learn three cauterizations in this shape and this measure exactly on the liver below the ribs where the human arm ends.
And after each cauterization, it should be on the thickness of a finger, and the cauterization should be straight along the body and do not squeeze your hand with the cautery iron yes indeed.
And let the amount that is burned from the thickness of the skin be half, no more, and the sick person should stand on his feet, if he cannot stand, then he should be lying down with his legs stretched out and his arms raised, and this is the image of the cautery iron.
And you can cauterize these cauterizations with the scalpel-shaped cautery if you have a companion and proficiency in the craft, and beware lest you overdo the cauterization so that it burns all the skin, so that it burns the abdomen and reaches the intestines, for the skin there is thin, so know this.
The Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
A tumor in the liver treated with cupping.
If a fistula appears in the liver and you want to know if the tumor is in the liver flesh or in its peritoneum, then if it is in the liver flesh, the patient will feel heaviness and pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the peritoneum of the liver, there will be severe pain with sharpness, and you see that physicians have been unable to treat it, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on his side, then outline the tumor location with charcoal.
Then heat the iron over the fire, and this iron resembles a hoe, and this is its image. And cauterize it with one stroke until it burns all the skin and reaches to the peritoneum, so that the entire abscess comes out, then treat him with the treatment of fistulas until he heals.
And this type of cauterization should not be used except by one who has long practiced medicine and whose hands have performed these diseases repeatedly through experience, so then he proceeds to such work and leaving it to me is better.
The Twentieth Chapter.
Cauterization of the Suture.
The ancients described cauterization with the roots of ziraund for a cold suture in this way: take one long, dry root of ziraund, as long as you can find, and as thick as your finger, then soak it in oil and heat it in the fire. Then cauterize with one stroke between the attachment of the clavicle and the neck, and two small strokes a little away from the armpits, leaning towards the side under the chin, and two large strokes above the breasts between the third and fourth ribs.
And two strokes also between the fifth and sixth ribs, leaning slightly backwards, and one stroke in the middle of the chest and another above the stomach, and three strokes from behind, one between the shoulders and two on either side of the spine below the cauterization that is between the wrists.
It is not proper that your hand should go deep into the abscess, but it should be on the surface of the skin with a probe; and some of the ancients have mentioned that there are people who use an iron cauterizer resembling a hoe and heat it and insert it between the ribs until they reach the tumor itself.
And it is removed as we have mentioned in the case of a liver abscess, and in this incision made with a probe from pus, either the patient dies within an hour or else there appears at the site a sore that does not heal.
Chapter thirty.
Concerning the spleen.
If you treated the spleen ailment with what we have mentioned as treatment in the classification, and your treatment did not take effect, then probing it has three aspects, all of which are correct: one is that you cauterize it with three probes or four arranged along the length of the spleen.
In the shape of the probes for the liver, which we mentioned the shape of before; and there should be between each probe and the next the thickness of a finger or slightly more. And the nature of the cauterizer is as we mentioned in the case of probing the liver.  And do not go deep into the spleen with the probe, and the posture of the patient lying on his back.
And the other aspect is in the elbow; you raise the skin opposite the spleen where the left arm of the patient ends, and you raise the skin opposite the spleen where the right arm of the patient ends, and your raising of the skin should be across the body so that the probes fall along the length of the body.
Then you insert the three probes very carefully until they pass through the skin on the other side, and then you withdraw the cauterizer so that there are four probes; and if you wish, you may cauterize with the other cauterizer which has three probes.
Then you treat the site of the probe after leaving it to drain pus for many days; this is better than all other treatments that have been mentioned.
Chapter Thirty-one.
On the Treatment of Hydrops.
The cauterization is effective in hydrops, especially the watery kind, if the patient who has been treated with the treatments mentioned above did not benefit from them, then it is necessary to apply four cauterizations around the navel and one on the abdomen.
And another cauterization on the liver and one on the spleen, two behind his back between the ribs, one in front of his chest and one in front of his abdomen, and the depth of the cauterization should be almost equal to the thickness of the skin, then the cauterization is left open to allow for pus drainage for a long time.
And do not neglect the patient after cauterization with the necessary treatment so that the appropriate medicines are gathered for him and his recovery is expedited, and the shape of the cauterizing iron used on the back is like what has been mentioned before, and the one used to cauterize the back is olive-shaped.
Chapter Thirty-two.
On Cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
If they swell in hydrops and are filled with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the notch between the thumb and the next toe.
And press your hand with the cauterizing iron and do not move it, then raise your hand and do not return it at all, because it drains the yellow water, and the cauterization iron should be like this shape.
Then cauterize the legs, two on each leg, and the cauterization should be with the blunt end of the iron, and the cauterization on each thigh should be two, one below the knee and another lower than that towards the middle of the leg, and on each thigh two cauterizations.
And leave the cauterization open without treatment for a long time, draining the water from it, then treat it with all that has been mentioned.
Chapter thirty-three.
Regarding the treatment of diarrhea.
If diarrhea is from cold and moisture until it weakens the forces holding and digesting in the stomach and intestines, and this was treated with various treatments but did not heal, and I saw the patient likely to die, I would perform a large enema on his abdomen. As mentioned above in the enema of the stomach with a circular  instrument and four enemas around the navel, I would use the gentle nail instrument, and an enema on the cotton on top of the coccyx large or two.
If I saw the moisture abundant and the patient likely to die from that, I would perform an enema on the anus and an enema on each rib cage, and perhaps two smaller enemas on the abdomen near the large one; for this is a successful treatment which does not err in its benefit if Allah wills.
Chapter thirty-four.
Regarding the enema for hemorrhoids of the anus.
If there are chronic hemorrhoids in the anus, many or one, and they are from thick cold humors or putrid moisture, and treated with what was mentioned in the classification but the treatment did not benefit, I would perform three enemas on the patient's lower back under the table slightly triangular.
And an enema under the navel with about two fingers, and if I judged that his stomach had become cold and his food was not digesting and I saw his face swollen, I would perform a large enema on the abdomen as mentioned above and an enema on his liver. And another on his spleen with a nail instrument, and I would leave the enema open for some time then treat him until he heals if Allah wills.
Chapter thirty-five.
Regarding the treatment of warts.
After cutting them if the wart was cut, take the instrument resembling a file and insert it into the same cut wart with your hand until the instrument reaches the mouth of the sweat gland from which blood flows, do this once or twice.
If the warts are numerous, then cauterize each one as described above and treat it with an ointment suitable for it until it heals. If the cautery is also done with cotton wool, this is more beneficial.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
Of cauteries for those in the buttocks and its surroundings.
If the ailment does not respond to the incision and procedure described in its place, then perhaps it will heal with cauterization. If one of the sores happens, and pus and foul humors flow from it, the first thing you should do is measure it with a fine probe.
Then, know the depth of its pit with the probe, then take a hot iron that resembles a plum and insert it cautiously into the same sore in a straight line along the depth of the sore and to the extent the probe entered. Repeat the cauterization until all those foul substances are burned once or twice or three times, depending on your need.
And be careful not to burn a nerve if there is one or a large sweat duct, and if the sore leads to the bladder or the intestines.
So be careful of all these places, but do this only if the sore is in a fleshy place and you have assessed that it is not penetrating. Then treat the area until it heals. If the area closes, its discharge stops, and it remains so for a while, know that it has healed completely.
And if its discharge does not stop, know that it is penetrating or has a rotten bone deep within it or something similar to what will be mentioned in its place.
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
Of cauteries for the kidneys.
If a pain in the kidney occurs from cold or a severe wind and as a result, there is a lack of sexual desire for the patient, it is necessary to cauterize it on the lower back above the same kidney with an iron cautery like the one mentioned before. Perhaps you can even cauterize it three times on the same spot, so that three cauterizations are aligned, which is more beneficial.
The Thirty-Eighth Chapter
In the case of bladder stones.
If weakness and relaxation occur in the bladder due to cold and moisture until the patient is unable to retain urine, make a cautery below the navel on the bladder where the beginning of the pubic hair starts and another cautery on the right side of the navel and another on the left.
And after the cautery on each side, make it the size of a thumb knuckle and form a cautery below the lower back or two cauteries if needed, and the cauterization implement should be as previously described.
The Thirty-Ninth Chapter
In the case of a uterus cautery.
If a substance of cold and moisture occurs in the uterus, by which it refrains from the umbilical cord and spoils its milk, and its cervix becomes difficult to pass, or if she experiences pain upon urination, it is necessary to cauterize three cauteries around the navel as mentioned in the bladder cautery. And a cautery on the cotton below the lower back or two, and the cauterization implement should be as previously described.
The Fortieth Chapter
In the case of a hip joint cautery.
Mucous fluids may accumulate in the hip joint, which causes dislocation and its sign is that one leg appears longer than the other when placed together, and you feel a gap in the location of the dislocation. It is necessary to cauterize the patient on the hip joint itself in a shape similar to a circle.
After learning about the hip with the pencil as it revolves, let the same hip fall in the center of the circle and the cauterization implement which is shown in the stomach cautery should be used. If this cauterization implement is not available for you, make three cauteries with the large olive-colored cauterization implement.
And direct the cautery to a depth equal to the thickness of the entire skin, then treat it until it heals, God willing.
Chapter forty-one.
Concerning sciatica.
If pain occurs in the area of the hip and its cause is cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated with what was mentioned in the previous division but to no avail, and time passes, it becomes necessary for the physician to soften the thick humors with a poultice of henbane or quince seeds or something similar.
Then, he should apply a warm compress and direct the treatment toward two things: either a treatment with stimulating drugs or a treatment with fire. The treatment with fire has many forms, one of which is to cauterize the area of the hip itself with three applications in this form.
And it should be made with a suitable depth, and the distance between each cauterization should be equal to the thickness of a finger. The cautery should be olive-shaped. And one cauterization may be applied in the middle on the top of the hip itself, so that there are four cauterizations. If you wish, apply one cauterization in the circle that was mentioned previously in the treatment for relieving the hip.
So that the circle encompasses the entire hip and burns through the entire thickness of the skin. This is the method for cauterization in sciatica if the pain is persistent to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, then apply two cauterizations on the thigh at the location indicated by the patient as painful, and one cautery above the ankle four finger widths toward the outer side, slightly. The cautery should be like a thin blade, and the depth of the cauterization should be equal to the thickness of the skin only.
And if he indicates that the pain extends toward the toes of the foot, apply cauterization where he indicates, with three or four or more applications as needed. And if he indicates the pain below the knee towards the leg, apply one cautery there like a thin blade.
Be cautious in all your cauterizations so that you do not reach the nerve or a large artery, lest you cause harm to the patient, either through a bad wound or illness.
And I have seen one and two who were cauterized above the ankle and burned in the cauterization, so that the leg became swollen until it reached the foot and all of it festered and decayed, then diarrhea occurred followed by death. If the pain is on both sides, cauterize them both in this way.
And some of the wise men have mentioned in cauterizing the hip, that this is how it should be done: a vessel resembling a cup is made from iron and its diameter is half a cubit. At its mouth, it should be slightly thicker than a date pit or a little less, and inside that cup there is another cup and a third.
And what is between each two cups should be the size of a thumb's joint, and the cups should be open on both sides and their height should be about a fist or two fists, and they take handles from iron that are tightly fitted to the cups, and this is its form.
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red and sparks fly, then it is placed on the right hip of the patient, who leans on his healthy side. Three cauterizations are made, round in one go, then it is left for three days, bandaged with butter, and the wound is left open for days.
Then it is treated with ointment until it heals, said the author of this book, this type of cauterization is rarely used because of its strangeness and its awful appearance, and few are those who can endure it except that it is good cauterization for whoever endures it and is afflicted in its place.
As for cauterization with burning medicines, it is made by making two cups resembling the one that descends into the mouth of a baboon from copper or iron.
There will be a rise in their edges of the height of two knots or so, and there will be after that between them the thickness of a finger, and it will be open at the bottom, open at the top, and some of it will have grasped each other like this.
Then you bring it down to the right hip, and the patient lies on his healthy side, and you tighten your hand firmly, then pour between the two circles hot water, which is warmed by fire, and hold it for an hour of sand, and the patient endures its prickling and burning, for he feels a burn like fire.
Until the prickling subsides, then you raise your hand with the instrument and wipe away the hot water from the whole hip with fresh water, then leave him for three days and apply butter to it until the blackness of the burn disappears, and leave him for days until pus flows from it, for this is more beneficial.
Then you treat him with ointments until he heals, but if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a plaster for him like what was made for the hip, which holds water, and this is the description of the hot water, which I have proven in the treatise on the rectification of medicines.
Take from the salt of the kidney and lime, unquenched, one part of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot that has been pierced at the bottom with a small hole the size of what enters through it, and place under the base of the pot another pot mixed.
And pour on the kidney and lime fresh water to cover them with a finger after you have firmly mixed them with your hand, and leave the pot until the hot water descends into the bottom of the mixed pot, then collect all that water and pour it onto another lime and kidney, renewing them as well.
For it becomes at that time very powerful in its intensity, and is used in many medical procedures and for treating all other parts of the body because it does the work of fire itself. And some medicines are also used to treat the hip with it, such as  thaffsia, honey from the balder tree, and lime mixed with soap, finely ground.
Galen claimed a story about an ancient man who treated pain in the hip and sciatica, greatly exaggerating the matter and claiming it did not need any other treatment and that it cured him at once.
He may have even entered the bath carrying him and came out cured. It is to be taken from the green shiraaj, but if the green one is not found, the fresh dry one is taken, finely ground with some tallow, and placed on the hip where the pain is or in the leg or thigh.
It is tightened and left for three hours or as long as the patient feels stillness in the burning, then he is entered into the bath, and if his body is relaxed, he is entered into the basin, for the pain goes away and it is cured by God's permission. If it does not heal, the poultice is repeated on him after ten days once more.
For it is cured if God wills, and know that it is not fitting for anyone to use these remedies except after emptying the body. Dioscorides mentioned that the goat's sweat when cauterized with it benefitted sciatica.
And the cauterization is like this: wool is taken and soaked in old oil and placed on the deep place between the thumb of the hand and the wrist, which is closer to the wrist, then take dry goat's sweat.
Then ignite it with fire until it becomes a coal and place it on the wool and leave it until it goes out, then take another one and continue doing this until the feeling reaches the middle of the arm to the hip and the pain subsides by God's permission. This type of cauterization is called the goat's sweat cauterization.
Chapter Forty-Second.
Cauterization for Back Pain.
Pain in the back may occur from many causes, either due to a fall or blow or excessive vomiting and the like, and it is from the outflow of cold, moist matter, and cauterization is only done in this type alone.
If a cold substance has been applied, after emptying the patient's stomach with ginger and the like, it is necessary to roast him on his back where the pain is, three rows in the same width as the table. After learning the location with lead in every row five portions or more according to what you see of the patient's condition and strength.
And the portion is with a point iron, and if you wish roast it three or four portions with an average nail-studded iron like this picture.
Chapter Three Thirty.
In a portion starting the hump.
This ailment is often found in young children, and its sign at the beginning in a child is shortness of breath when standing up and moving, and you find in the last vertebrae of the back a bead that has protruded, exceeding all other beads.
If you see this and want to stop it, roast it with an iron that is circular like this picture. To take the portion on each side of the vertebra evenly, and if you wish, roast it around the vertebra with a point iron two or three rows, and let the points be close to each other, then treat the location until it heals as mentioned.
And beware that you use the portion in the hump that is from the tightening of the nerve.
Chapter Four Forty.
In a portion for gout and joint pain.
If the pain of the joints is from cold dampness that settles into any member of the body, and if the pain occurs in the legs, it is customary for physicians to call that gout especially.
So if the cold gout is treated with the types of treatment mentioned in the division, and the pain does not go away, then the portion removes it, which is to roast after emptying around the joint of the legs many portions, and the iron is medium-sized olive color like this picture.
And if you need to cauterize on the face of a man, do so with a cautery point. If the pain ascends to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, apply to each knee three or four times from each side with this olive-colored cautery alone.
And if you need more than this cautery, apply it and do not plunge your hand deep with the cautery but make it about the thickness of the skin only. If the pain ascends to the hips or back, use what we have mentioned from the cautery in its chapter.
And if the pain is in the hands only, cauterize around the wrists as two circles turn. If the pain remains in the fingers, cauterize each knuckle and on the palm of the hand. If the pain ascends after days to the elbows or armpits.
Then cauterize them from each side and let not the sick be deprived of good care and taking medicines, for if he has good food and expels phlegm, he will heal with this cautery, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Fifth.
On Cauterizing a Fistula.
If a hernia appears in the groin and some of the intestines and stool descend to the testicle, and this is beginning near, it behooves you to order the sick man to leave off eating for a day and that he use laxatives which bring down the feces from his belly.
Then he should lie between your hands on his back and order him to hold himself until the stool or intestine protrudes, then return it with your finger and then learn by lead under the hernia on the pubic bone a mark resembling half a circle with its sides toward the top of the body.
Then heat the cautery, shaped like this.
Until it comes white and throws sparks, then return the intestine or stool into his belly, then a servant puts his hand on the place so that the intestines do not protrude, and you have loosened between the sick man's legs and placed a cushion under him and another servant binds around his legs.
And another on his chest holds his hands then the iron comes down on the same mark and your hand with the iron standing straight holding it until it reaches the bone or you return it again if it does not reach the bone in the first time.
And be cautious of your effort from the protrusion of the intestines while you are cauterizing lest you burn it and thereby cause to the sick either death or a great affliction, and know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work has not succeeded, and it is necessary that the cautery for young boys be gentle on their bones and for the elderly on their bones.
Then you treat the place of the cautery after three days with butter until the dryness of fire goes away and then treat it with all ointments until it heals, and let the sick be lying on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you make his food during his treatment the following in order to keep his stomach tight so that the intestines do not protrude when he belches and flatulence then if he wants to stand after forty days, you use a firm bandage and hold it for another forty days and lessen from fatigue and fullness from food and drink and excessive shouting.
For if he uses this arrangement thus, he will heal completely, God willing, and I will mention the treatment of a hernia by cutting into it in its chapter, God willing. As for the hernia that occurs in the rest of the abdomen and was just beginning, if you want it to not increase, cauterize the hernia with a rounded iron according to its size. And let what you burn from the skin be like one third of it, then treat it with what we have mentioned, for it will not increase, God willing. And some of the ancients have mentioned that they cauterize the hernia with a three-pronged iron in this form.
After you have learned on the hernia with the cautery and make the line that is in the side at the upper part of the hernia, and the other line to the bottom, and you descend your hand in the middle with one cauterizing iron, and the first cautery is easier and best, God willing.
Chapter Sixty-Four.
In the treatment of ulcers.
If in some members a drop or strike happens, and the pain from that lasts for a long time, and there is no cure with medicine, then it is necessary to cauterize the point with a soldering iron and make the cauterization of each member according to its size, whether large or small, its weakness and its strength.
And if the pain and the ulcer are cured from the first cauterization, otherwise, repeat the cauterization because it is customary for these pains to transfer from the member to what is near it, so it is necessary to follow them with the cauterization until the sick person heals.
Chapter Seventy-Four.
In the treatment of leprosy.
As for those suffering from leprosy, they benefit greatly from cauterization, especially the type of leprosy that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and black bile.
If you want to cauterize someone, if the leprosy is just beginning and you treated it with what we mentioned in the section, and it did not subside and did not stop, and you fear that corruption will take over all of the patient's constitution, then cauterize the head five times. One in the center of the head as is customary, and the second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two on the temples, and one from behind on the nape of the neck, and be careful with the cauterization a little until it affects the bone slightly.
And remove the scales from it to make it easier to breathe the thick vapors from it, and cauterize it in the same way on the spleen as mentioned before. As for if the leprosy has persisted on the patient and appeared clearly, then it is necessary to cauterize these cauterizations that we mentioned in the head. And cauterize on the tip of the nose, and two on the cheeks, and two on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the coccyx at the end of the tailbone, and another above it in the same position, and two on the shins on each leg, one. Two on each knee, two on each ankle, two on each elbow, and two on the armpits, and he shapes it over every joint of his fingers and toes, and on every heel of his feet and hands.
And he takes care from the nerve that is on the back of the heels so as not to burn them, and it may cauterize a little over the pubic bone, and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver, and know that every time you increase cauterization it is more beneficial and better.
And know that the sick person does not find pain for cauterization as the healthy person finds it because his body has been numbed, and it is necessary that the cauterizations be of large or small size according to the organs and joints according to what has come before from the qualities of the instruments.
Then he treats cauterization with a fine linen cloth with honey and all other treatment until it heals, if Allah wills.
The 84th Chapter.
In cauterization for numbness, when a member of the limbs has been treated with medicines, ointments, and bandages but did not heal, then cauterize the same numbed limb with cauterizations according to what it deserves, based on the size of the bone or its smallness, and let your cauterizations be slightly thicker in the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it with an ointment until it heals, and it may cauterize for some numbness that occurs in the hand and foot in the vertebrae of the back at the exit of the nerve that moves that limb, so that the numbness goes away.
And do not proceed with it except for one who is knowledgeable about the anatomy of the organs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
The 94th Chapter.
In cauterization for leprosy.
If leprosy has become old and no cure from the arts of medicine has benefited it, then cauterize on it with cauterizations in its depth a little according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with finely ground lentils, with rose oil, the tongue of a lamb, and the blood of a pigeon or a quail, one part of each, mixing them all together and applying them to a cloth and bandaging the site until it heals.
The Fiftieth Chapter.
On the Crab (Cancer).
If the cancer is just beginning and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a circular iron around it as it revolves. Some sages have mentioned cauterizing a blunt instrument in its center, but I do not see that because I expect it to be scorched and I have seen this happen several times.
So the right thing is to cauterize around it with a circle as we said, or with many small cauterizations.
The Sixty-First Chapter.
On the Cautery of the Scab (or Tumor).
If a scab occurs and it delays in ripening, either because of the force that brought it about, or because of the age of the sick person if he is elderly and has little blood, or because of time, and you want to speed up the ripening of the scab, cauterize around it with many small cauterizations, dropping them.
Then leave it and it will speed up the ripening. If you want to apply a larger cauterization, heat the iron whose shape is shown.
And bring it down to the center of the scab until it pierces the skin, and let the cauterization be from below so that the pus flows easily, then treat it as appropriate until it heals.
The Seventy-Second Chapter.
On Cauterizing a Eating (Ulcer)
An eating (ulcer) is a corruption that advances in the limb and eats it, as fire consumes dry wood. If you see an eating in a place suitable for cauterization with fire, heat many small and large nail-shaped cauterizations according to what suits that location where the eating is.
Then you should remove it from every direction until all the corruption is eradicated and nothing of it remains at all, then leave it alone for three days and apply to the burnt areas sulfur powder mixed with oil until all the scabs and all the corruption are removed.
Then treat it with the healing ointments for flesh; if you see after three days that the flesh is growing healthy growth with no corruption, otherwise repeat the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted areas, and some ulcers may be treated with a strong medicine.
Because it acts as fire, more rapidly beneficial; I mentioned its treatment with a strong medicine in the section, so take it from there whenever you need it.
Chapter thirty-five.
Cauterizing Nails, Upright and Inverted.
This ailment frequently occurs in the soles of the feet, a rough thing that troubles the man; and cauterization is done on two types: either by fire cauterization or by hot water cauterization.
As for cauterization by fire, it is to heat a curved iron instrument resembling an eagle's feather, made of iron to enclose the nail on all sides as much as possible and have a thin edge; then place it over the nail and turn your hand with the instrument around the nail until the instrument reaches the depth of the nail.
And leave it for three days to become covered with pus; then bandage it with a piece of dough made from flour, pounded with salt, and leave the bandage on it for one night; for it will come loose from its roots, then treat the wound site with a healing ointment for flesh until it heals, if the nails are not inverted.
And this frequently occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet; so it is necessary to take a tube of copper or iron or an eagle's feather, place it over the nail or wart, and then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube.
Hold your hand and as you turn it with a slight movement of your wrist, so that the edge of the tube acts upon the root of the screw, and the sharp water finds its way to penetrate the root of the screw, and let the patient endure for a little while the prickling of the sharp water for an hour.
Then leave it, for the screw will be extracted with its roots. Thus do you act with each one until you come to all that is in the body, then treat the places after they are extracted by what grows flesh from ointments.
The Forty-Fifth Chapter.
On treating a fistula.
If a fistula occurs from cold in the nerve or from fever of a quarter or otherwise, it is necessary to make four or five cauterizations on the spine bone between each vertebra a cauterization and in its chest a cauterization. And on his belly, a cauterization with the olive iron so that the fistula subsides and accelerates the ripening of the cold disease.
The Fifty-Fifth Chapter.
On treating a bruise that occurs in the body.
A tumor may appear on the body that is unsightly, caused by cold, thick, and rotten materials, so when it first appears, you should cauterize on the top of each tumor a gentle cautery with an iron rod whose tip has been ignited with fire or with a long willow twig's root or with a lens cauterizer.
And you cauterize the tumors at their first appearance in this manner, so that it does not increase and the useful effect is dispersed from it and the patient heals, except that this should be done after the patient has bled.
The Sixty-Fifth Chapter.
On treating bleeding that occurs when an artery is cut.
Often, bleeding occurs from an artery that has been cut during a wound that is exposed from the outside or when cutting a tumor or cauterizing a member, and so on, making it difficult to stop its flow.
If this happens to anyone, hasten with your hand to the artery's mouth and place your index finger upon it and pull it tightly until you constrict the blood under your finger so that nothing comes out of it. Then put in the fire small and large olive-seed kernels several and heat them until they become very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery opened, and put the hot kernel on the same vein after you have quickly removed your finger and hold the kernel until the blood stops.
If blood surges when you lift your finger from the artery's mouth and the kernel cools, take another kernel quickly from the prepared ones in the fire and continue doing so with one after another until the blood stops.
Be careful not to burn a nerve, which could cause another affliction for the patient. Know that if an artery bleeds from it, it cannot be cut at all, especially if it is large, except in one of four ways: either by cauterization as we mentioned, or by amputation if it has not already been amputated. For if it is amputated, its ends contract and the blood stops, or else it is tied with strong threads, or else medications are applied to it that have the effect of stopping blood and tightening with bandages tightly.
As for those who try to cut it with a ligature or by tightening with thread or applying burning things and the like, blood does not stop entirely except rarely. If this happens to anyone and a doctor and medicine are not available, he should hasten to put his index finger on the mouth of the wound itself as we described.
And pull it tightly until the blood constricts and leaks from above the wound, and the finger does not remove from it with cold water always until the blood freezes and thickens and stops, and during that time, look at what is needed for cauterization or medicine.
Chapter Two.
On incisions, drainage, venesection, and similar operations.
Al-Khalf said, "We mentioned in the first chapter every illness that is treated with cauterization by fire and corrosive medication, its causes and reasons, instruments, types of cauterizations, and I made that into chapters from the top to the bottom."
And I follow in this chapter the same path so that it is easy for the student what they seek.
Before I begin with that, it is necessary for you to know, O sons of mine, that this chapter contains more difficult matters than what is in the first chapter regarding cauterization.
And for that reason, it is necessary for the warning to be stricter because the work in this chapter often involves draining blood which is the basis of life when opening a vein or making an incision on a tumor or abscess, or treating a surgery, or removing an arrow or cutting open a stone and similar things which accompany all of them with danger and fear and death occurs more often in most of them.
And I advise you to avoid falling into what is doubtful because in this profession, kinds of people with different illnesses may come to you, some who have become weary from their illness and death has become easy for them.
Because of the severity of what he finds from his disease and the length of his suffering, and with the illness being so close to death, and some who spend their wealth on you in hope of health, and their illness is a struggle, so it is not right for you to help those who are like this at all.
And let your caution be greater than your desire and eagerness, and do not proceed with anything from that except after knowledge that is certain to you of what happens to the blessed outcome, and use in all treatment of your illnesses, advancement of knowledge and warning of what leads to safety.
