For in that you have assistance in acquiring praise and glory, mention and thanks, may God guide you, O sons of mine, and not deprive you of truthfulness and success, for that is in His hand, there is no god but Him.
I have arranged this chapter into sections according to what was mentioned in the chapter on the types of wounds from the front to the back so that it would be easier for you to find what you want from it, God willing.
The first section.
In the treatment of water that collects in the heads of boys.
This ailment often afflicts boys at birth if the midwife presses the head of the boy without gentleness, and it can also occur from a hidden cause that is unknown.
I have not seen this ailment in anyone other than boys, and all those I saw among them died quickly, so I saw fit to leave treatment for it.  I also saw a boy whose head was filled with water, and the head grew larger every day. Until the boy could no longer sit on himself because of the size of his head, and the moisture increased until he died.
This moisture is either collected between the skin and bone or collected under the bone on the peritoneum, and the treatment for it if the moisture is between the skin and bone and the swelling is small, then a single incision should be made in the middle of the head, one across, with a length of about two spans until the moisture drains. And this is the image of the scalpel.
If the moisture is more and the swelling is larger, make it two incisions intersecting on this pattern:
And if the moisture is under the bone, and its sign is to see the sutures of the head open from every direction, and the water decreases if you press it with your hand inwards, this should not be hidden from you, then three incisions should be made in the middle of the head on this pattern:
And after the incision, all of the moisture comes out, then the incisions are closed with thread and bandages, and it is anointed from above with syrup and oil until the fifth day, then the bandage is removed and the wound is treated with gauze and ointments, and do not leave the head tightened moderately, and feed the patient with all dry food, little moisture.
Until the member becomes strong and healed, another recipe for incision is to look where the bone of the tumor appears and the water gathers because it may be in the back of the head or in its front or on the right or on the left.
So, by incision, it is meant where you see the tumor and fullness of water, so you cut it as much as you can, and be cautious not to cut a vein so that bleeding does not occur and the patient dies from that bleeding along with the discharge of moisture.
Chapter Two.
Cutting the two arteries behind the ears known as the jugulars.
When a sharp ailment is presented to the eyes or chest and it persists for a time and medicine has not helped, then the treatment in this case is to cut these two arteries.
When you want to cut them, first shave the patient's head with a razor then rub the place with a rough cloth so that the artery appears, then tighten the patient's neck by his garment, and look where the pulse is and their places, the two hidden places behind the ears. And rarely are they hidden except in some people.
Then mark them with the pencil and cut them with the scalpel, a cut to the bone, and this should be across the head, if you wish, insert the scalpel from under the artery and sever it upwards by cutting, and the length of the cut should be about two fingers squeezed together.
If the pulse stops, blood will flow out with a pulsating flow that rises forward in a steady stream. If the artery does not appear to the touch, it is necessary to determine from the ear after a distance of three fingers then mark it with the pencil and cut to the bone, and what is necessary.
Send from the blood six ounces in total and perhaps you send more or less all of that according to what appears to you from the strength of the patient and fullness of his arteries, then look at the wound if anything remains on the bone from the peritoneum cut it.
That it may not present a hot tumor and then tighten the wound with a thread of coarse linen, then treat it with ointments until it heals.
The Third Chapter.
In the two arteries that are in the fingers.
If it happens to a person with chronic sciatica or acute attacks from the effects of hot and humid moisture in the muscles of the fingers or chronic severe headaches, and he was treated with various medical treatments but it did not benefit him, then we have tried in these diseases  cutting the arteries of the fingers or cauterizing them as we have described.
And the way of working in cutting them is to shave the hair that is on the fingers, and we mean the visible artery in the temple because it becomes apparent to you from its pulse and rarely is it hidden except for individuals among people.
Or if in the case of extreme cold it is hidden from you, let the patient  tighten his neck with the help of his garment and then rub the place with a cloth or cover the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly visible. Then take the scalpel whose picture is this. Then you dissect it gently with it until you reach the artery, then you throw a snare into it and pull it upward until you bring it out of the skin and free it from the membranes that are underneath it on all sides, if the artery is thin, bend it with the tip of the snare. Then you cut off a part from it as much as the distance between its ends contracts and does not cause bleeding, for if it was not amputated and severed, the blood did not flow at all, then empty the blood from six hours to three.
If the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong doubled thread, let the thread be either from silk or from bowstrings so that it does not quickly become infected before the wound heals and bleeding occurs.
Then cut the surplus between the tendons, do that immediately or after a while, and if you wish to mold it like bone with a thin iron scalpel until its edges become smooth, it will perform this task as well or even better as we have mentioned.
Unless the patient has a fever or an imbalance of humors, because molding helps to eliminate fluids and is more beneficial in this case, after cutting both arteries it is necessary to pack the site with tightly wound lint and place a firm dressing on top. After healing, treat with dry medicinal plants that promote tissue growth and a poultice until healed, God willing.
If bleeding from the artery occurs during your work, immediately cut it either with a scalpel or fill the site with stibium and tighten your hand until the blood stops. If you have neither of these, place your finger to stop the blood flow.
Wash the site with very cold water until the pain subsides and tighten it as necessary. And what is easier and simpler than cutting the artery, is molding the vein with this double-edged scalpel after marking the locations with lead.
And lower it deeply until it reaches the bone, and the vein cuts in two places so that the distance between its ends is widened because it will not fuse with this molding at all, and this is a picture of the scalpel.
The sharpness of the blades resembles two small daggers except that they are much less sharp than a scalpel because if they were as sharp as the knife, coldness would reach them faster and the flesh wouldn't stop bleeding quickly; and if there is some thickness to them, hot fire will stick to them.
And it cuts flesh quickly, and this work is better than all works and lighter and easier, let there be a thickness between the blades equal to the thickness of a finger.
Chapter Four.
In the treatment of hot, constant tearing from the eyes.
If the tears are constant and their flow is from the veins on the skull from outside and there was no benefit in treating it with medicine and you saw the face of the sick person become red. And he feels on his forehead a buzzing like the crawling of ants and his eyes are sunken, wet, with their eyelids swollen and thickened from the intensity of the tears, so they were forced in treating them to this work, which is called treatment by the sword, which is that you order the sick person to shave the hair on his forehead.
Then you make three parallel incisions on the forehead, along the length of the forehead, with each incision about two finger widths long, one parallel to the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, the second a short distance from the movement of the muscle in the temple, and the third on the other side.
And be careful not to cut the two arteries on the sides, and keep your hand away from the contact of the jaws, with each incision being three finger widths apart, and have at your disposal pieces of sponge prepared or a large amount of dry cloth to absorb the blood.
Then you insert the sharp-pointed scalpel whose image is this. From the incision following the temple to the middle incision, and you scrape with it all the skin that is between the incisions, along with the peritoneum on the bone, then you do the same from the middle incision to the third incision, and then you extract this scalpel. And you insert into the first incision another tool called a sharp-edged scalpel, blunt on one side and sharp on the other, whose image is: .
And you make its sharp side upwards towards the flesh adhered to the skin and its smooth side towards the bone, and you push it until it reaches the middle incision, cutting with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes without reaching the outer skin.
Then you do that in the middle incision to the other incision, and after blood has flowed moderately, you squeeze the places of clotted blood. Then you place a piece of cotton thread in each incision and put on top of it a pad soaked with wine or oil or vinegar and oil.
So that a hot tumor does not occur and on the third day, the bandage is removed and a large amount of poultice with warm water is used, then it is treated with a balm of baslikon with rose oil and all that is used to treat wounds until it heals, God willing.
The Fifth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Tears and Discharge from the Eyes from Within the Head.
When one has a copious, acute, painful, constant discharge from the eyes and sees two small spots of pus from them and his vision is weak and his eyelids are ulcerated and the eyelashes fall out from them. And there is a severe, painful headache deep in the head and persistent sneezing.  Know from these symptoms that those substances and discharges come from many deep veins, and the best treatment for it is this treatment, which is to order the patient to shave his forehead and then make one incision in the middle of the forehead.
And there is a severe, painful headache deep in the head and persistent sneezing.  Know from these symptoms that those substances and discharges come from many deep veins, and the best treatment for it is this treatment, which is to order the patient to shave his forehead and then make one incision in the middle of the forehead. Or raise it slightly in breadth and begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, making the incision to the bone, and keep your hand away from the muscle of the temples that move when chewing until the bone is exposed and all the blood is wiped with a sponge.
Then separate the edges of the incision with soft cotton or a linen thread, and then pull it taut from above with pads and soak the pads with wine and oil so that a hot tumor does not occur. When you have removed them and see that the hot tumor has broken, it is necessary to scrape the bone until flesh begins to grow in it.
Then treat it with the drying preparation that causes flesh to grow, such as taking two parts of wheat flour and four parts of calamine powder, preparing a balm from them, and using it for the growth of flesh in such wounds.
Chapter Six.
In the treatment of what falls into the ear.
All that falls into the ear is one of four types: either a mineral stone or something like stone, such as iron and glass, or a plant seed such as chickpeas, kernels, and the like, or a fluid thing such as water, vinegar, and the like.
Or an animal, so if a stone or kind of stone fell into the ear that does not exceed in the ear, receive it with sunlight, then if you see the stone, put something of  a scent from violet oil or sandalwood in it, then try to remove it by moving your head or wiping it with a swab. And plug the nostrils when sneezing comes after placing a band of linen or wool around the ear and stretching the ear upwards, then often it exits with this treatment, if it does not exit, then try to remove it with a soft cotton swab like in this image.
If it exits with the swab, otherwise try to remove it with a blind probe that is soft and slightly flexible, if it does not exit by this means, then make a tube of copper and insert one end of the tube into the hole in the ear yes.
And plug what is around the tube with dough mixed with oil so that there is no way for air other than the tube, then pull it with your breath with a strong and repeated pull, often it exits by this means, if it does not exit by what we described, otherwise take from the Nabataean chew or the pointed chew used to catch birds, something small and place it on the tip of the probe.
After wrapping a tight cotton around it and inserting it gently into the ear hole after drying the ear from moisture, if it does not exit by all that we described, then hasten to the incision before a hot swelling or congestion occurs.
The incision prescription is to make a small incision in the scalp first and extract the blood from it according to its strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn their ear upwards and make a small incision at the root of the ear near its fatty tissue in the lower position.
The incision should be crescent-shaped until you reach the stone, then remove it with whatever instruments you can manage. Then sew up the incision as quickly as possible and treat it until it heals.
As for if the thing that has fallen into the ear is one of the grains that swell and become inflated, try to remove it with what we have mentioned. If it does not come out, then take a delicate and fine scalpel in this manner.
And try to cut that kind of grain that has fallen into the ear with it. But only do this if you are certain that the grain has become soaked with the ear's vapor until it becomes small pieces, then remove them with a blunt probe or a soft sponge or by sucking.
As we mentioned, it is easy to remove them. As for water that has entered the ear, it is necessary to use a  clogged cotton swab first, and after filling the ear with some fluffy cotton while lying on that ear containing the water if it exits by that.
Otherwise, take many pebbles along your fingers, smooth and delicate, warm them slightly with fire, and insert one of them into the hole in his ear, and he grasps his leg with that side, and strikes a stone with the stone in his ear.
So he continues to do this with pebble after pebble until all the water comes out. It may also come out by taking a reed or feather, inserting one end into the ear, and heating the other end until it burns mostly, then replacing it with another feather.
Do this several times until all the water comes out, or draw it out with the tube as we mentioned before in the case of the pebble. As for removing an animal that has entered there, look if it is small like a flea and similar. Treat it with what we mentioned in the section. But
If its body is large enough to be felt, try to remove it with a sponge and probes. It is easier than all that happens in the ear.  As for removing the worm born in the ear if you have treated it with what we mentioned in the section on earwax and your treatment did not help
It is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun, if something appears to you from the worm, then take it out with a probe or with fine forceps. If nothing appears to you from it, then take a tube like this one's form.
Narrow at the bottom and wide at the top, and insert the slender end into the ear as much as the patient can bear, then grasp it with a firm grip and do this several times until all the worm comes out. If it does not yield to coming out, seal around the tube with wax as I mentioned to you in the pebble.
If it does not come out with what we mentioned, use the catheters I mentioned that the ancients used to kill the worm and you will find that in the article of the catheters. And pouring medicines into the ear with this tool is like its form:
As you see, it is made of silver or copper, narrow at the bottom with a small hole and wide at the top. And if you wish for the projectile in the tube's belly to be of well-fitted brass, or if you wish, take mercury and wind cotton tightly around its tip.
Then pour the oil or juice or whatever you wish of these medicines into the tube while it is in the ear, then insert the mercury with cotton from above and squeeze it with your hand, squeezing moderately until the oil rushes into the inner ear and feels it.
With the patient inside, let what is poured into the ear be warmed slightly in the fire and beware that the thing being dropped into it be not very cold or very hot, for the ear cannot withstand that.
The Seventh Chapter.
In treating the temporary obstruction of the ear.
Some children may be born from their mothers with their ears unpierced.
And it may also happen to some people that there is an obstruction in the ear canal from a wound or flesh growing there, and this obstruction may be deep inside the ear's opening, invisible to the eye.
Sometimes it may be slightly visible outside the hole, and can be seen by the eye. That which is in the depth of the ear and cannot be seen by the eye, in most cases, is difficult to remove. And that which can be seen should have the ear of the patient placed in the sun. And look at it, and if you see the obstruction visible, open it with a gentle scalpel, the shape of which is:
Its tip has a slight projection, limited somewhat, and the rest of the scalpel is smooth on both sides so that it does not harm the ear. If the obstruction is from flesh that has grown in the passage of the ear, then grasp it with a gentle clamp and cut it gently, firmly until all the flesh is removed.
If the obstruction is in the depth of the ear, take a gentle, smooth probe and warm it slightly in the fire, then insert it into the passage of the ear. If you feel the obstruction and the patient feels heaviness of hearing, then push against it gently.
And be careful not to injure the nerve of the ear, then put a wick in the ear, commensurate with the size of the hole, which has been dipped in Egyptian ointment. Do this for days until you are safe from the wound closing or take a wick and moisten it in water and sprinkle powdered saffron on it.
Use it, and if you see the ear has swollen and there is hot pus, then it is necessary to remove the wick and replace it with another wick that has been dipped in a preparation of rose oil until the hot swelling subsides, then treat it until it heals.
If bleeding occurs, dip a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use the rest of the treatment that stops the bleeding mentioned in the section on cauterization.
The Eighth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Warts that Appear in the Eyelids.
These blemishes which appear in the eyelids may be moist and dry, so it is necessary to grasp them with a forceps or a pincer and cut them from their roots with a scalpel, then apply powdered lead on the site.
If blood flows from it, cauterize it with a delicate lentil-shaped iron and cover it best after the cut, and often it returns if something remains of its roots, and if cauterized by fire, those roots are burnt and do not return.
The Ninth Chapter.
In treating cold arising in the eyelids.
Often, a thing resembling cold in intensity and hardness appears in the eyelids.
Therefore, it is called cold, which is the gathering of thick moisture in the upper and lower eyelids, and the action taken in it is to look, if the cold mass is protruding on the outside of the eyelid, it moves to every direction so its matter is easy, then cut a slit across it.
Then gently exfoliate it from every side until it is removed, then suspend it with the forceps and cut it, if it did not become ready to be cut except after the eyelid passes through the cut, it does not harm the patient at all, and if the slit is large, collect it by sewing, and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, there is no harm in it, for the ointment will mend it and heal it, and if the cold mass leans towards the inside of the eyelid towards the inner surface, turn the eyelid and suspend the cold mass with a forceps without needing to make a slit, and cut it from every side.
If the eyelid passes through the cut, it does not harm at all, then wash the eye after cutting the cold mass with salt water and treat the site with what heals until the ailment is healed.
The Tenth Chapter.
In treating pterygium which appears in the eyelid.
Pterygium is a growth in the layers of the upper eyelid, and it appears more frequently in boys. It weighs down their eyes and exposes them to discharges in the mornings, and they are unable to look at sunlight. So that tears flow rapidly towards them.
Therefore, they are always leaning on their faces and sleeping on them, and their eyelids are under the eyebrows wet with swelling and the pterygium is clearly visible to the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers, you feel the pterygium between them, and the procedure is to place the patient's head in a block.
Then take a linen cloth and prepare a wick from it, and make a circle from that wick corresponding to the extent of the pterygium on each side, then place it on it and press it with your fingers on each side to gather the pterygium in the center of the circle.
Then, make a cut in the center of that moisture with a scalpel, a longitudinal cut, and the cut should not be larger than the incision made in bloodletting. As for depth, you should cut through all the skin until you reach the pterygium.
In most cases, the pterygium protrudes from the incision in the form of a white fatty piece. You pull it out with a cloth wrapped between your fingers to the outside while you turn your hand right and left until it is completely removed. Beware that you do not increase the incision lest the scalpel pierce the eye and harm it.
If the pterygium does not appear in the first incision, it is necessary to increase the incision slightly gently until the pterygium appears, then pull it out as we have said, and then soak a cloth in vinegar and water and place it on the site and hold it gently, and some people crush salt.
and place it in the incision to dissolve what remains of that moisture, then treat him until it heals. If a hot tumor occurs at the site, treat it with soothing poultices until it heals,.
Chapter Eleven.
Types of Eyelid Stitches.
If hair grows in the eyelid exceeding its natural course under the normal eyelids and it is tightened, it harms the eye and causes various diseases such as continuous tearing, relaxation of the eyelids, whiteness, and thickening until this becomes a cause for blindness.
And eye stitches are of four kinds: either by cauterizing with fire, or by a sharp medicinal agent as mentioned previously in the chapter on cauterization, or it is by cutting and stitching, or by using a reed, as I will describe later.
It is necessary to make the patient's head on your stone, then turn the eyelid with your left hand if it turns, otherwise, insert a needle in it with a thread from below the eyelid and pass the needle with the thread from above near the hair itself, and pull the thread upward to the eyelid.
Then turn it with the needle, and then cut into the inside of the eyelid without the excess hair with a knife from the larger opening to the smaller one, then guide the thread and place under the eyelid a small pad of cotton or linen, and then apply to the eyelid with a pencil.
Like the shape of a fig leaf, except that the shape should be to the extent you want to raise the eyelid because it may differ among people, some need to cut from the eyelid a suitable amount according to how relaxed the eyelid is.
And some need less cutting, all of it according to the relaxation of the eyelid, then cut with a knife along the two lines I have taught you and begin from the larger opening to the smaller one, and the incision should be near the natural hair like the thickness of the needle.
Then insert the thread into one of the corners of the skin, then guide it through all of it, and gather the edges with a needle and fine wool thread, wipe away the blood, and stick what remains of the threads on the eyebrows with some fine things.
If you wish to do this, otherwise it is of no consequence, then the suture and thread are left for about three or four days, then it is treated, and if you wish, you leave the wound without suturing and treat it with what dries and contracts; for the eyelid rises when the wound is sealed and joined together, and suturing is better.
This face of the tashmir was mentioned by the ancients, except that it is a burden on the patient and it is good work and there is no danger in it, and another face in tashmir also, which is to learn on the eyelid a shape like the shape of a sycamore leaf as we described. Then the eyelid is raised with three supports that are spaced apart or grouped in this image:
Then what remains of the eyelid is cut with a small pair of scissors in this image, cutting moderately.
If you cannot hold the supports and it does not suit you, take a needle with thread and insert it in the center of the shape and insert another thread near the larger aperture and a third thread near the smaller aperture, and gather the threads together with your fingers moderately, then raise it with them a moderate raising.
And raise the skin that is attached to it all, as we described, then gather the edges of the wound with the suture and treat it until it heals. If a hot tumor appears when you cut or split it, soothe that tumor with qairot (turmeric) and its like from soothing ointments.
And the lower eyelid may also be exposed to the turning of its edges, so it is necessary to use what we mentioned from cutting, suturing, and cauterization with fire and sharp medicine; cauterization with fire or sharp medicine is more effective and easier on the patient than cutting and suturing, and cutting and suturing are both finer.
Cauterization with cane is like this: turn the eyelid and cut the incision from inside as described, then make two or three thin pieces of wood whose length is equal to the length of the eyelid and their width is less than the width of a scalpel.
And I have placed in the edges of both sides where the threads adhere, then gather them together gently on what is left of the eyelid and tighten the two parts from both sides tightly, and leave it for days, for the stretched skin dies and darkens and decays.
Until it falls off by itself, if you delay, then cut it with the scissors and treat it until it heals. If it joins, the eyelid rises and the eyelashes do not fall from the eye, and this is the image of the two parts that you make in this shape and amount in length and width precisely.
The Twelfth Chapter.
On raising the eyelashes that have fallen from the eye with a needle.
If it is one or two hairs to work on that, take a fine needle and thread it with a thin, smooth silk thread, then gather its ends and tie them in a very fine knot, and let the length of the thread be about a span.
Then, thread another thin thread into the  lash and put it in the middle of the base, tie its ends if you wish. Then place the patient's head on a stone near the sun so that the work is clear, for it is delicate work, then insert the needle with the lash into the root of the extra hair.
And thread it into the eyelid quickly until it comes out above the natural hair, then pull the thread up towards the lash and insert that lash if it is one or two or three, no more.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the lash in the eyelid along with the natural hair. If you pulled the lash and did not bring the hair out with it, pull the lash down with the thread you put into it until the lash comes out from the upper hole.
Then put the hair back in and pull both of them, do this until it rises in the upper hole and you see it with the eye. Then release the lash and thread and take them out and tighten the eyelid and leave it tight for two or three days until the hair stays in place and flesh grows on it.
If the hair is short, either add to it a long hair of natural hair so that it rises with it, or leave it until it grows longer after a time, then raise it.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
On the Treatment of Hairs that Grow in the Upper Eyelid.
The condition these hairs cause is called an arnab, and these hairs can be either natural or acquired. The acquired ones result from the closure of a wound or scar, such as from a cut or puncture.
And the way to treat it is to cut that closure and separate its sides, making a thread of cotton between them, and tying it until it heals. One should not use things that dry and constrict in its treatment.
If you do that, the hair will return worse than it was. Instead, use things that soften it, such as fenugreek, a poultice of flaxseed with a little bit of saffron mixed in water, and Diachilon ointment which is diluted with a little fat, applied to the wound, and treat with it.
And the goal of its treatment is to try every means possible to prevent it from healing in the same way it was originally. This work we have mentioned is only some repair of the hair, not returning the area to how it was before.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
On the Treatment of Hairs that Grow in the Lower Eyelid.
These hairs that grow from the lower eyelid are truly called "shtera." They can be either natural or acquired. Acquired ones result from a wound, cut, or puncture.
And the way to treat it is to take a needle with doubled thread, insert it into the flesh, and pass it from the left edge to the right edge until the thread reaches both sides of the flesh. Then, stretch the flesh upward with the needle and cut it with a wide scalpel.
If the shape of the eyelid returns to what is proper, and if not, take a needle and place it in the position of the incision and turn the eyelid with it and make two incisions on the inner side of the eyelid and make the ends of the incisions from the angles of the cut that was made until they meet, so that there is an angle. Until when they come together it becomes shaped like this shape.
And it is the Greek letter lamad, then remove that flesh as much as the sharp side of it is lower than what is below the eyelid, then gather the separated parts with two stitches sew it with wool thread and then treat it with what we mentioned from softening and ointment until it heals.
And if the eyelid is exposed from an incision or suture or elsewhere, then it is necessary to make a simple incision without eyelashes as mentioned above and then separate the lips with ointment as mentioned.
And the general rule in treating the eyelid if it is from above or below is that work is done on it according to what appears to you of the shape of the eyelid, for it can be diverse in its image and the craftsman adapts the means in any way he is able.
Until the shape returns to its natural form or approaches it, and the same illness tells you what is suitable for it from work and tools in most cases.
The fifteenth chapter.
In the adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or to the cornea.
This adhesion may occur to many people, that the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye, preventing it from moving easily and hindering its natural actions, so it is necessary to insert the tip of a needle under the eyelid.
And lift it up or extend it with a wire, then cut the adhesion with a gentle scalpel that is not sharp like the edge of the scalpel but rather a little so as not to alarm the patient when working, and the scalpel slips and injures the eye with its sharpness, and the cutting is as if you are peeling off that adhesion.
And expect that when the eyelid returns to its natural form and all the adhesion is healed, you should pour into the eye salt water to wash it or instill in it from the ginger-colored saffron solution diluted with water, then separate between the eyelid and the eye with a cotton thread.
And you place on top of the eye a cloth soaked in egg white and after the third day, use the ground saffron until it heals.
The sixteenth chapter.
In cutting off the nail and removing the flesh of the eyelids.
The nail is of two kinds, either it is nervous and resembles a thin, firm membrane, or it is not nervous and resembles solidified white moisture; if iron touches it or it is thrown into the fire, it breaks when grasped by tongs.
And no tongs have been proven to be effective on it, and both types begin from the larger part of the eyelid until they gradually grow thin, covering the eye completely and preventing light and movement; and the method of work in cutting it is to place the patient's head on a block.
Then he opens his eyes and lifts the eyelid with your hand, then you take tongs that are slightly curved and extend them upwards, then take a needle and insert a hair from a horse or cows mane into it along with strong thread; bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the middle of the nail.
And you push it through with the needle and tie the nail with thread, extending it upwards; then you peel away the side of the nail next to the pupil with the hair as if you are spreading it with the hair to the end, then cut the remaining part at the base of the eyelid with a fine scalpel or small scissors, leaving the natural flesh of the eyelid.
So that it does not cause constant tearing from its cut, and the nail may be extended with tongs alone or with thread as we have said, then peeled away with the smooth scalpel, the end of which is pictured:
Be cautious that the knife does not touch the corneal membrane, for this will cause inflammation of the pupil, and after cutting, something of powdered salt or zanjabeel should be placed in the eye, and it is left until another day, then it is treated as appropriate until it heals.
If the wart is not nervous and it was impossible to insert a needle into it or fix a snare in it, this type of wart is often treated with medicine and heals as described in the division. And if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye.
Take a gentle, smooth scalpel with a weak edge as shown here: . And scrape the wart with it gently, from above, and if you see that it is breaking apart and crumbling, and its trace was only by scraping, then place something of zanjabeel, or red zanjabeel, or powdered salt in the eye, and pull the eyelid for a day.
Then repeat the process until all of it disappears, except if a hot tumor appears in the eye, then leave it and treat the hot tumor until it heals, then repeat the scraping process until it heals. And as for a piece of fleshy meat...
If the piece of flesh hurts the eye painfully, then tie that piece with a snare and cut some of it, but do not overdo the cutting so that tearing will occur, then instill red zanjabeel or zanjabeel into the sockets until it heals.
Chapter Seventeen.
In cutting the  eye-wart and what grows from excess flesh in the eye.
Some people may have red flesh growing in their eyes, piled on top of each other until it covers the sight or comes close to it or overflows onto the eyelids, and perhaps the eyelids turn outward resembling a jasmine flower.
And the treatment for it is that the patient places his head in a block and then opens his eyes, and all of that red flesh is captured with the snares corresponding to it.
Hold it with forceps or a probe, then cut the first layer of flesh until all of it is cut away, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation. Your cutting can be done either with the scalpel described for cutting the nail or with small scissors. like those used to pick up wool as it comes out, its form being shown in the chapter that follows this one.
And when you have finished cutting and all of the wool has gone, fill the eye with powdered salt or instill in it a few drops of red ochre or such like soothing medications, and place a pad made from white egg yolk over the eye to prevent inflammation.
And if some wool remains and the bleeding is excessive and you fear inflammation, leave the eye and treat it with something that soothes inflammation, then return to the operation when it has healed. Do likewise with any excess flesh exposed in the eye from this type.
Except that it is necessary for you to avoid treating any weak eye either by natural means or by surgical operation, and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that the organ is capable of withstanding it.
Chapter Eighteen.
On Removing Wool from the Eye.
Wool are red veins that grow on the eye, obstructing vision and weakening the eye with the passage of time. It is necessary for you first to examine, if the eye affected by wool is strong and there is no other ailment in it besides the wool.
Then the operation, which is to command the patient to place his head in a block and then attach those veins with one or two threads, according to your skill, and the threads should be fine and flexible in this form:
or two threads joined together into one body in this form:
Then grasp those veins with a fine pair of scissors gently, and wipe away the blood every now and then until you see that the eye has been cleared of the wool and the bleeding has stopped. Take care not to injure the eye with the edges of the scissors, and let your work be done in the middle of the day facing the sun.
Be steadfast in your work, so that you do not cut any other veins; when finished, put a green or red scalpel into the eye to eat up what remains of the vessels. If you cannot remove all of it at that moment, then apply something to the eye that will soothe the pain.
Leave it for days until the pain subsides and the hot swelling is gone, then repeat the operation on this same spot until this image of the painful cutting disappears.
Leave it [and have the head of the patient in the apprentice's lap and the other wiping away the tears and looking into the front and back of the eye and you] The original method for the operation is to open the eye with a fixed or triangular tool held by an apprentice.
Pierce [and have the head of the patient in the apprentice's lap and the other wiping away the tears and looking into the front and back of the eye and you] You can choose to start cutting from the top or bottom of the eye, but it is preferable to wipe away two pairs of folds in the upper arch; one at the end of the halo and the other at its beginning.
Hold them between the middle and index fingers, then attach folds from underneath opposite them; then grasp them between the ring finger and little finger, and move your hand lightly until you see all the vessels raised, cut from the smaller west end with a scalpel if it is visible, and with a fine knife otherwise.
Then insert the tip on a needle and carefully sever all the vessels until they are raised on the membrane, and do not cut off the weeping because the tears and blood will mix (and confuse) you.
Then cut with the scalpel what remains beyond the halo, both above and below so that no more is left except on the cornea; if you can raise it from the cornea, scrape with the tip, for this is better, and it may be easier in some people.
And if you cut it, let it heal for days until the pain subsides and the hot swelling is gone, then repeat the operation on it.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
In the Setting of the Feather in the Nose.
Physicians call a feather "nasoura" if they treat it with cauterization or a strong, burning medicine as described previously, and if it does not heal, there is no remedy except to split the swelling when it ripens and extract all of its moisture or pus.
Until the bone becomes exposed. And if, when it is exposed, you see corruption or blackness in it, remove it with an instrument whose image is:
And it is called "the head rasp" and it is made of Indian iron, and its head is rounded like a grain, with the inscription of a scraper or a scalpel carved finely. You place it on the site of the corruption in the bone, then rotate it between your fingers as you gently squeeze your hand until you feel that the corruption has been removed.
And you do this several times, then cover the place with drying and astringent medicines. If the place is closed and flesh grows in it and the flow stops, and remains for forty days without recurrence or suppuration, and no incident occurs within it.
Then know that it has healed, otherwise there is no remedy except to return the "nasoura" to the nostril opening in this manner: expose the bone again with iron or a burning medicine. And if the bone is exposed, take a swab on this image:
Its tip is triangular and its shaft is conical, drawn to the tip as you see it, then place it on the bone itself, and that should be near the nostril, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then rotate your hand with the swab until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it.
Until he feels the wind coming out of it, if he holds his hand over his nose, then cover the place with astringent and drying medicines as I have taught you. If flesh grows and the place hardens, then the material that was protruding outwards returns to the nose, and this will be easier on the patient, God willing.
Chapter Twenty
The Treatment of a  Prolapse of the Eye.
If the eye protrudes in its entirety and there is no defect or loss of vision, it is necessary to ease the patient then dissect it in the scalp and place a bandage on the back of the head without condition and suck out pus with a thin tube.
Then, place on the eye a poultice made from acacia gum, spikenard, frankincense, and cloves, then tighten the eye from above onto the bandage with many pads. The prescription for the pads is to take many soft cloths and fold each one four times to make many.
Then, place them one on top of the other according to what the eye needs, then tighten them with a firm cloth firmly and reapply the bandage with a thin tube without condition. Then remove the bandage and leave the eye tightened for a day and night.
If the bandage relaxes during that time, it is necessary to tighten it again. Then remove the bandage after a day and night as we said. If you see that the eye has returned, otherwise, repeat the bandage, pads, tightening, and suction until it returns.
Chapter Twenty-One
The Treatment of a  Cut on the Eyelid
If there is a hernia in the eyelid layer, and it protrudes and appears outside the eyelids like an olive, deforming the human image, and you want to cut it, then proceed as I describe.
Which is to insert a needle into the base of the hernia from below upwards, then insert another needle with doubled thread from the side of the eye socket and pass it through. Leave the first needle as it is.
Then, cut the place where the doubled thread bends and tie some of the hernia to the needle tightly. Then remove the needle and place cotton wool soaked in egg white on the eye and leave it until the threads fall off with the hernia. Then treat the eye with something that strengthens it.
Until the wound heals, and one may tighten the bandage from every side with a circle of cloth until the eye becomes more comfortable, then it is cut with a fine scalpel reaching to the depth of the eye so that the white discharge flows out and the eye descends and dries on its place, then tighten it until it heals.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
In the Treatment of a Canker Sore.
This ailment called a canker sore is when matter gathers in the eye resembling flowing water but without it. The procedure for this is to make the patient sit on an upright chair, then take his head from both sides with your hands.
And move him until you see the matter descend to the bottom with your eye, then stabilize and it will not leave and light will proceed and the patient will see things as he used to, and if it does not descend to the bottom we know that it is water. And if the matter does not happen to descend as mentioned.
Otherwise, make the patient sit in front of you, then take a fine scalpel and cut with it above the cornea slightly at the junction of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the circle until the matter comes out.
Then if it comes out, instill into the eye hot water which has been mixed with honey or water that has been boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
The Twenty-Third Chapter.
We have mentioned the types of water in the classification and which one is suitable for irrigation with a detailed and explained explanation, so take it from there on the right track. Then, you should make the patient sit in front of you upright facing the light near the sun.
And bind his healthy eye tightly, then raise the eyelid of his eye with your left hand if the eye that has water is the left eye or with your right hand if the right eye.
Then you place the point of the probe near the edge of the white of the eye from the direction of the smaller pupil, and push the probe forcefully while turning it with your hand until it penetrates into the white of the eye, and you feel that the probe has reached something empty.
The depth of the probe's insertion should be equal to the distance from the pupil to the end of the black, which is the edge of the eye. The copper [speculum] allows you to see inside the eye because of the clarity of the cornea. Then you turn the probe upwards to the place where the water is.
Then you press it downwards repeatedly. If the water comes down from its chamber, the patient sees what has opened for him from his chamber and the probe in his eye. Then he rests a little. If the water rises, lower it again without withdrawing the probe.
If it settles and does not rise, withdraw the probe gently while you slightly loosen its hold with your hand. Then dissolve a little of pure salt in the water and wash the eye from within. Then place over the entire eye outside a poultice or wet wool.
Anoint it with rosewater and egg white and bind the healthy eye over it. As for us and people of our time, we place ground cumin mixed with egg white on top. If the probe does not enter the eye because of its hardness, as some people's eyes are very hard. Where you should take the scalpel called "the bridle," whose image is:
Then you pierce it with this instrument only, and do not overdo the piercing; rather,  you should aim for a gentle spot for the probe, then introduce the probe as mentioned before. When your work is complete, prepare the patient lying down firmly on his back in a dark room.
And he refrains from all movement and coughing, and you make his food what softens his nature, nor does he move his head to the right or left at all, and the bandage remains on him until the third day, then you uncover him in that dark room and test his sight.
Show him things then return the bandage on the seventh day and it is not permissible to do this during the time of treatment or after the removal of your cauldron from your hour but it is necessary to avoid this before the water rises quickly by careful looking.
If a hot swelling appears then it is necessary to release the eye before the seventh day and  repair that with what soothes the swelling until when it has subsided then at that time you release his sight and place on his face a blindfold which trains his sight from beneath for days while he is in that dark house then.
He exits from the house gradually and behaves in his affairs, and know that the cauldron is not dispensed with by the learner without viewing it several times then he proceeds to work.  And it reached me about some of the Iraqis that he mentioned that he makes in Iraq a useful cauldron which absorbs water.
