The Twenty-fourth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Flesh Growing in the Nose.
Flesh of various kinds may grow in the nose, some of it resembling scorpions with many legs, and some of it being cancerous flesh hardened like the color of mud, and some of it being soft flesh not like the color of mud.
As for the flesh of this kind that is soft and not malignant or cancerous, it is necessary to make the patient sit before you facing the sun and open his nostril and place the snare in that flesh and then pull it out and cut what you have grasped from it with a sharp, delicate scalpel on one side.
Until you know that all the flesh has gone, and if anything remains of it that you were unable to cut, remove it with one of the delicate instruments gently so that nothing remains of it. If blood overwhelms you or a hot swelling appears.
Treat it with what is appropriate, or if it was from malignant tumors, be swift in cutting it until the blood stops and all flesh disappears, then place it inside the nose after cutting, empty or with water or drink, and if the nose opens up and moisture flows from it to the throat.
Know that it is cured, if the moisture does not flow as it should, know that inside it there is flesh growing in the upper part of the loose bone and the instrument did not reach it with the cutting, so then it becomes necessary to take a thread of linen with some thickness.
And tie it with many knots, making between each knot the size of a finger or less, and make it possible for the patient to insert one end of the thread into his nose with a rod or whatever he can after making it like a bead, and pull on its breath until it reaches the nasal cavity.
And it comes out on his throat, and often the boys do such things in school, which is easy for him who desires it, then gather the two ends of the thread, one end that came out of the mouth and the other that remained in the nose.
Then use the flesh-spreading with the knots on the thread, do this until you know that the flesh has been cut by the thread of the knot, then take out the thread and it becomes in the nose after wiping the blood a wick soaked in Egyptian ointment, do this for three days or more.
Until the ointment eats up all that remains of the flesh, then the last thing in the nose becomes a lead pipe for days until it heals, if it needs treatment to dry it out, that is what you use.
And this is a picture of the instrument with which drops medicine into the nose:
It is made from silver or brass, like a small candlestick, open at the tip and with a passage as well.
And if you wish, make the tube closed like a pipe, and the tip of the instrument flat.
It has a handle at its end as you see, and one grasps it when it is heated with oil or whatever juices or flowing things you wish.
The twenty-fifth chapter.
In the ingrowing pimples on the tip of the nose.
Many times a pimple grows on the tip of the nose, and it increases and becomes larger with the days until its appearance is ugly.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut it at its first appearance and remove all of it, then apply to the place either cauterization or a burning medicine that takes the place of cauterization, if you missed cutting it until it becomes large, look if it is hardened, solid, pale in color and little feeling.
Then do not expose it to iron, for it is a cancerous tumor and I have seen many who had this tumor cut from them and returned with a great affliction on their owner, if the tumor is soft to the touch, not pale in color, and you see that the cutting can be done throughout. Then empty the patient and cut it without hesitation or delay, and treat the place with what dries and contracts until it heals.
The twenty-sixth chapter.
In sewing the nose, lip, and ear. If the connection of them is separated from a wound or something like that, know that when a separation of connection occurs in one of these cartilages, there is little that is beneficial to do in most people.
It is necessary that when one of these things is presented, look if the wound is fresh with blood, then you gather the edges of the wound with stitching and treat it until it heals, but if the separation of the connection has separated its edges and each incision has become correct, it is necessary to peel each incision with the thickness of its outer skin until it bleeds.
Then gather the edges with stitching and tighten them, and apply a mixture of mastic and frankincense powder on it, and place above the layers a patch of palm ointment or another similar soothing ointment and leave it tightened for two or three days then remove it.
The medicine is changed and left until the threads separate of themselves, then it is treated with an ointment until it heals. The description of suturing is to gather the separated parts either with needles as we described in suturing the abdomen or with thread as we have informed you about there.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
On extracting a cyst that appears in the lips.
Many people may present to you with small, firm growths inside their lips, some resembling a wart and others smaller or larger. It is necessary to turn the lip inside out and make an incision over each cyst, and then tie it off with a thread.
And it is cut on each side, then the place after the cutting is stuffed with powdered sulfur until the bleeding stops, and then rinsed with vinegar, salt, and the places are treated with what you have mentioned until the wounds heal.
Chapter Twenty-Eight.
On cutting excess flesh in the gums.
Often, excess flesh grows on the gums that the ancients call a "boil," so it is necessary to tie it off with thread or grasp it with forceps and cut it at its root, and leave it to bleed for a while, then place powdered sulfur on the spot.
Or one of the clamping, drying cautery instruments, if that flesh returns after treatment, it often comes back so cut it again and cauterize it, for it does not return after cauterization.
Chapter Twenty-Nine.
On filing teeth with iron.
There may gather on the surfaces of the teeth, both inside and outside, and between the gums, rough, ugly scales which may darken, yellow, and green until that brings about decay to the gums and disfigures the teeth because of this.
So it is necessary to make the patient sit in front of you with his head in a block and file down the molars and teeth on which you see scales and things resembling sand until nothing remains of them, and do the same for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and the like until they are cleaned.
If the matter inside it has gone from the first incision, or else you repeat the incision on it another day and a second time and a third until you reach the goal of what you desire. And know that the molar tooth requires different shapes of drills many forms according to what appears for your work.
For the drill that drills a molar from within is not the same as the drill that drills it from the outside, and the one that drills between molars is of another form. And these are several forms of drills that will be with you all prepared.
Chapter Thirty.
On Extracting Teeth.
It is necessary to treat the tooth for its pain with every method and delay its extraction because it has no replacement if it is pulled out, for it is a precious element, even if there is no alternative but to extract it.
And if the patient insists on its extraction, then you must ensure that the painful tooth is healthy. For often the patient is deceived by the pain and thinks that it is in the healthy tooth, so he extracts it, and then the pain does not go away until the diseased tooth is extracted. We have seen this many times done by barbers.
If the painful tooth is healthy in your opinion, then you must cut around the tooth with a scalpel that has some strength until it separates from the gums on every side and then move it with your fingers or with forceps gently at first little by little until it loosens.
Then when that happens, you can grip it with the large forceps securely and the patient's head between your knees so that he does not move and then pull the tooth in a straight line lest it break. If it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from each side gently and rock it as you did first.
And if the tooth is hollowed or broken, then it is necessary to fill that hole with a strip of cloth and seal it well with the tip of a thin instrument lest it be torn while you pull on it with forceps, and it is necessary that you carefully examine the gum around it from every side.
Be cautious in your effort so that you do not break it, and some of it remains, returning on the patient a harm greater than his first pain.  And beware of doing what ignorant barbers do in bridge-building and boldness in attacking a fortress without using what we have described.
For often they inflict great harms on people, some of which is that a tooth breaks and its root or part of it remains. Or, if he pulls out part of the jawbone as we have seen many times, and then gargles after pulling it out with vinegar or salt water, if bleeding occurs from the place, often this happens, so that at that time something of alum is ground and put in the place.
And if this is not useful to you,  take it. If the kallalip images that move the tooth first are long-handed, short-handled and thick so as not to bend when grasped by them on the tooth, and these are images of the large kallalip:
Be as you see, thick handles so that when you grasp them they do not give themselves nor bend. Short in length, and let it be of Indian steel or well-forged iron with fixed ends. And at its end are teeth which enter into each other so that it grips tightly and securely.
And the ends can be made in the form of a clamp, also becoming strong for clamping.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
On the Extraction of Tooth Roots and Removal of Broken Jaw Bones.
If, when extracting a tooth, the root remains broken, it is necessary to place cotton soaked in grease on the site for a day or two until the area relaxes, then you insert the  (givet) or (khalilib). Which resemble the beaks of birds called bulraqjah. This is a picture of the khalilib:
It is made like a clamp from the inside or like a (asklifag). If these khalilibs do not help you to remove it, then you must excavate around the root and expose all the flesh with a scalpel, then insert the instrument that resembles a small  (attala), which is pictured:
Short in the end, slightly thick, and not fixed so that it does not break. If the root comes out with this, otherwise use these other instruments, which are pictured: The first is triangular at the end, with some thickness:
Another picture of a delicate triangle:
And we may also use this instrument with the two prongs, which is also pictured:
And without others of the instruments and tools mentioned before in the list of tooth extractions. We may also use this instrument that resembles a large (sannarah), which is pictured:
Triangular in end, curved, with a little thickness so that it does not break, and not fixed. Know that the instruments for teeth are numerous, as well as all other tools, they are almost uncountable. The skilled artisan in his work may invent for himself instruments according to what the work and the diseases themselves indicate.
Because some diseases were not mentioned by the ancients due to the diversity of their types, if a bone of the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth is fractured or suppurates, search for it in its place with what is suitable from among these instruments and probes that were mentioned for extracting roots.
And we assist ourselves with a graft of its image:.
It should be somewhat thick so that it can control the bone and not escape until the bone comes out, and we force the place with appropriate medications, if the bone has slight pus, cleanse it of its pus and blackness until it is purified, then treat it until it heals.
The second thirty-third chapter.
On planting teeth that have sprouted on others.
If the molars sprout on a path other than their natural course, they become deformed thereby, especially if this happens to women and slaves, it is necessary to look, if the molar has sprouted behind another tooth.
And if it was unable to grow or be returned, remove it, if it is stuck with another tooth, cut it with this instrument whose image is:
And it resembles a small beak, and let it be from very sharp Indian steel, and let your cutting of it be over many days because of the hardness of the tooth, so that it will not shake any other teeth, as for if it is coming out with a strong root, remove its root with a scraper from India whose image is:
It is all from India, and its tip is very finely engraved, it is like the scraper used to make needles, with it, gently scrape the tooth little by little over many days so that the tooth does not shake and fall, then smooth it afterwards and remove its root with some pliers.
And if a tooth has broken off from it, and it hurt the tongue when speaking, it is necessary to scrape it also until the roughness of that break disappears and it becomes level and smooth so that it does not hurt the tongue or spoil speech.
Chapter Thirty-three.
In wiring loose teeth with silver threads or gold threads.
If the front teeth are shaken and move from a blow or fall, and the patient cannot bite on anything to eat lest they should fall out, and they have been treated with astringent drugs but there was no benefit in treatment.
The remedy is to tie them with a gold or silver thread, and gold is better because silver tarnishes and rots after days, while gold remains as it is forever, and it will not be subject to that. The thread should be of medium thickness, neither too thin nor too thick, according to what fits between the teeth.
And the image of wiring is to take the thread and insert its loop between the two sound teeth, then weave at both ends of the thread between the loose teeth, one or more, until the weaving reaches the sound tooth from the other side.
Then she weaves back to the side where she started and pulls her hand gently and wisely so that it does not move at all, and the tightening of the thread is at the roots of the teeth so that it does not come loose, then cut the ends of the excess thread with scissors and gather them together and tie them with a needle and hide them between the sound tooth and the loose tooth.
So that it does not harm the tongue, then leave it like this until the end, if it unravels or breaks, tighten it with another thread, and he will enjoy it like this for his whole life, and this is the image of the teeth and the form of wiring in two sound teeth and two loose teeth as you see:.
And the one tooth or two may return after falling in their place and be wired as we described and remain, but this is done by a skilled craftsman, and he may carve bone from ox bones to make it like a tooth and put it in the place where the tooth went. And he is tightened as we said and remains so and enjoys it .
Chapter Forty-Third.
In the cutting of the tether that appears under the tongue and prevents speech.
This tether that appears under the tongue may be natural, born with it by the human being, or it may be accidental from a wound that has healed.
And the work in it is that you open the mouth of the sick person and his head in your block and raise his tongue, then cut that nerve tether across until the tongue releases from its hold, if there was some stiffness and complexity in it and it was from a wound healing, then make a suture in it and cut it across until the tether is severed and the knot dissolves.
And beware that the cut is not in the depth of the flesh, so that a vein is cut there and blood appears, then gargle after the cut with rose water or vinegar and cold water, then place under the tongue a wick of cotton which the sick person holds every night.
So that it does not adhere together again, if bleeding occurs, put on the place powdered saffron, if the blood overcomes you, cauterize the area with a lens-shaped soldering iron suitable for this purpose. Then treat him with all treatment until he heals.
Chapter Fifty-Third.
In extracting the frog that is born under the tongue.
It may happen under the tongue, a tumor like a small frog that prevents the tongue from performing its natural function and perhaps grows until it fills the mouth, and the work in it is to open the mouth of the sick person facing the sun and look at the tumor.
If you see it as a dark color or black, solid and the sick person does not feel any sensation in it, do not treat it because it is cancer. If it tends towards whiteness and has moisture, make a suture in it and cut it with a fine scalpel and free it from all sides.
If blood overcomes you while working, put powdered alum on it until the bleeding stops, then return to your work until you complete it, and then rinse with vinegar and salt.
Then treat it with all appropriate remedies until it heals.
Chapter Thirty-Sixth.
On the Treatment of Swollen Tonsils.
And whatever grows in the throat from other tumors may appear inside the throat, glands that resemble the glands that appear outside and are called tonsils; if you treat it with what was mentioned in the classification and it did not heal.
Then look, if the tumor is hard like a dry color with little feeling, do not expose it to iron; and if it is red in color and its root is thick, do not also expose it to iron for fear of bleeding, but leave it until it matures, either that you will press it down or that it bursts from itself.
And if it is white in color, round, and its root is soft, this is what should be cut; and the work in it is to look before you work, whether it has calmed its heat completely or with some lessening.
Then, when that is the case, seat the sick person with his heel in the sun and his head in a block, and open his mouth, taking a servant between your hands, you press his tongue down with an instrument, its image is:
It is made from silver or copper and is thin like a blade; if you press it against the tongue, and the tumor becomes clear to you, take a pair of pliers, and insert them into the tonsil and pull them outwards as much as possible without pulling with them any part of the membranes.
Then cut it with an instrument, whose image is like scissors, but the ends of each are bent at a right angle to each other, very sharp, made from Indian iron or Damascus steel:
If this instrument is not available, then cut it with a scalpel. This is its picture:.
Sharp on one side and not sharp on the other. After you cut one almond, cut the other in this same type of cut, then after cutting, gargle the patient with cold water or vinegar and water.
If bleeding occurs, gargle with water that has been mixed with pomegranate rind or myrtle leaves or something similar until the bleeding stops. Then treat him until he heals.  Sometimes tumors may grow in the throat other than the almonds, so they are cut as described for cutting the almonds.
And I treated a woman from a tumor that had grown inside her throat, striking the palate slightly and nearly blocking her throat. The woman was breathing through a narrow passage and it had prevented her from eating or drinking water.
And she was close to death if she had lived another day or two. The tumor had risen from it, with two branches until they came out through her nostrils. I acted quickly and inserted a hook into one of them and pulled it, and a piece that was good was drawn out.
Then I cut it where I reached it from the nostril, and then did the same with what protruded from the other nostril. Then I opened her mouth and pressed down on her tongue, and inserted the hook into the tumor itself, and cut some of it away. Only a small amount of blood came out.
Then the woman's throat cleared, and she immediately started drinking water and then eating food. We did not stop cutting from that tumor repeatedly for a long time, and the tumor would replace what was cut until a long time passed for both of us.
Then it shriveled and the tumor inside the throat healed, so it stopped growing. Then she left, and I did not know what God had done to her after me.
Chapter thirty-seven.
On cutting a tumor of the scrotum.
A tumor that is called a fig if it descends into the scrotum and becomes swollen, and white, elongated in shape. If it is thick at the bottom and round, then it is called a fig. If treated with what has been mentioned in the classification, and treatment was not effective.
And I have seen the hot tumor subside from it and become soft, then it is necessary to cut it. And that which was from it, gathered round, and had no length, and was reddish or like blood color, or black, or had no sensation, then it is necessary to avoid cutting it.
So there is danger for the patient, so it is necessary if you see it in the description that was mentioned of its whiteness and length, to make the patient sit with his heel toward the sun and clamp his tongue with the instrument that will be described later, then insert the scalpel into the fig.
And pull it downwards and cut it with one of the two instruments that have been mentioned in cutting the tonsils, and it is necessary that you do not cut from it except what exceeds the natural state without more because if you cut more than that you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after the cutting, use what was described in cutting the tonsils and treat it until it heals. If the patient fears being cut, it is necessary to use the trick in healing it without fear or caution, and the direction of the treatment is with a sharp medicine, which is to place the head of the patient in his stone.
Then clamp his tongue with the instrument that was mentioned, then take from the sharp water that was mentioned in the chapter of treatment and knead it with a paste not extinguished, making it neither thick nor thin, and fill its cavity with this tool, and this is its image:.
Its end, where the medicine is placed, has a cavity like that of a spoon's bowl, and you place the instrument with the medicine on the scrotum itself, and the patient lies on his side so that saliva flows from him from inside his throat so that nothing falls down into his throat to harm him.
Then you hold your hand on the medicine while you crush it on the wound for half an hour until you see that it has darkened and the sting of the medicine has subsided. And if you wish to take cotton, you wrap it on the end of a rod and moisten the cotton in the medicine.
And you insert the rod with the cotton into a tube from above until it adheres to the wound. You do this repeatedly until you reach the desired amount of stuffing for the navel, then leave it; it will wither and fall off after three or four days. If you need to reapply the medicine, apply it again.
After stuffing, you wipe around the navel with cotton moistened in ghee and dry it with what surrounds it of the medicine, then rinse with cold water. It is treated externally with plasters and internally with gargles until it heals. This type of treatment is safer than cutting and further from fear.
And the navel can also be treated with something gentler than stuffing and cutting; it is treated with incense in this manner:  Take fennel, saffron, ginger, licorice, frankincense, marjoram, cumin, and similar herbs. Gather all of them or some of them in a pot and immerse them in vinegar.
And it is boiled while the pot is lined with clay and there is a hole in the middle of the lid. Upon this, a funnel-shaped instrument is placed, made of silver or copper:
And the end with the opening is inserted into the patient's mouth until steam ascends to the navel through the tube until the navel feels comfortably full, then it is repeated several times until it withers. And beware of making this treatment at the first occurrence of the swelling.
For it often increases the swelling. However, it is best to do this when the swelling has subsided and becomes less hot. If you do not have this instrument, take a tube and attach a piece of eggshell to its end so that the patient's mouth does not burn.
Because the eggshell prevents hot steam from burning the mouth and this is good treatment with safety.
The Thirty-Eighth Chapter.
In extracting thorns and anything that grows in the throat other than that.
Often a bone or thorn of fish or something else grows in the throat, so it is necessary to extract what is visible to the eye after pressing the tongue with the instrument at the sun (the uvula).
To make it clear to you what is in the throat, and if something does not appear to you and hides in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit before his food is digested in his stomach, for perhaps the thing that has grown will come out with the vomit or the patient may swallow a piece of bread or even a whole piece of  a date.
Or he may swallow a piece of dry bread or take a piece of soft sea sponge, tie it in a thread, then have him swallow it, and when it reaches the place of the thorn, pull the thread quickly, do this several times.
For often the thorn or bone sticks to it and comes out, but if it does not come out with what has been mentioned, then use an instrument of lead in this form:
It should be thicker than the reed slightly, and at its tip there is a hook that the patient inserts into his throat gently while raising his head, and he must be careful not to touch his larynx so that it does not cause him to cough, and pushes out the bone or thorn, or the physician can insert it with his hand.
And it is better for the patient to insert it himself so that he knows the place of the thing that has grown, and pushes down or pulls up with his hand on the instrument all that appears to him until it comes out.
The Thirty-Ninth Chapter.
In extracting a lodged lump in the throat.
If you have treated the clot with what was mentioned in the division of treatment with medicines and it has not been effective, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun after you have pressed his tongue with the tool that was described to you.
If your sight falls upon the clot, then draw it out with a small fishing line or a soft, tight cord. If you are unable to do so, then take a hollow pipe and insert it into the throat of the patient near the clot, then insert a piece of iron protected by fire into the inside of the pipe.
Do this several times, and have the patient abstain from water for the whole day, then he takes a container full of cold water and opens his mouth into it and gargles with it without swallowing a drop, and moves the water occasionally with his hand.
If the clot falls into place if it feels the water, then if it does not come out with what we have described, vaporize the throat with urine and with the halite by the instrument that was described in the incense of the leha, do this several times because it will fall.
And the way to work with incense is that you take a pot containing hot embers in the fire and the pot covered with a lid in its center has a hole, then put the tip of the instrument into that hole and throw the incense, and the patient puts his mouth on the end of the pipe and closes his mouth so that the incense does not come out until he knows that the incense has reached his throat.
If the clot falls into place, then if it does not fall, repeat the incense several times and have the patient endure thirst and eat salt and garlic and do not drink water, there is no doubt that it will come out with this arrangement, and this is a picture of an instrument that attracts the clot from the throat if it comes to sight.
And it resembles the kallalb as you see, except that it has this attachment that enters the throat and its ends resemble the beak of a bird in it is roughness if it bites on something it does not leave it:
And another instrument which is used to press down on the tongue, it is a wide ring of iron the size of the mouth, above the tongue, it enters the mouth standing on its side and the mouth remains open involuntarily for the patient and he cannot remove it at all until it is removed.
A description of the instrument which opens the mouth in this same manner.
The Forty Chapter.
In it there is a discussion of the cutting into tumors and splitting them.
Tumors have many diverse types, as will be mentioned one by one in this book, and they differ in their cutting into and splitting from two aspects: one from the nature of the tumor itself and what it contains of humors.
And the second type is from the places where they occur in the body, because the tumor that occurs in the head is not like the one that occurs in the buttocks, and the tumor that occurs in a fleshy place is not like the one that occurs in a joint, each one has its own ruling regarding the procedure.
And there are some tumors that should not be cut into until the pus inside them has matured and is complete, and there are others that should be cut into while they are still immature, such as tumors that are close to joints.
Because if a tumor occurs near a joint and lasts for a long time until it putrefies around it, it may corrupt the ligaments or nerves of that joint, so it becomes the cause of paralysis of that limb or the tumor is near an important organ.
Because if you delay cutting it until it matures, it may harm that important organ or it is near the buttocks so you cut it into while immature but it is necessary to cut into the immature tumor that is near the buttocks so that it does not rot and penetrate into inside the anus so that it becomes a fistula.
And it becomes in a way that does not heal, and it is necessary for you to know the time of cutting into tumors that have matured completely, which is when the pain of the tumor subsides and the fever disappears and the redness and throbbing decrease and the head of the tumor softens and all other signs.
It is necessary to place the knife at the lower point of the tumor if it is possible, so that it is easier for the fluid to flow downwards, or in the most depressed and protruding place of the tumor, and let the knife be going lengthwise with the body if the tumors are in the hands or feet.
And the places of the muscles and tendons and nerves and arteries, and in general all places that are flat and have no bending, but as for those that bend, let the knife go according to that place. But if the tumor is in fleshy places, it is best to leave it without a knife.
Until it ripens as we have said completely, for if you cut into it before that, the discharge from it would be long and full of pus and filth, and perhaps its lips would become hard and ulcerate. And some tumors may be cut across the body according to necessity or as the limb requires.
It is necessary to use a single knife for small tumors, and for large tumors a wide knife or many incisions according to the size of the tumor. And it may be that some tumors require the skin to be pulled taut and cut if it has become like a sheet.
And it may be that some tumors have died to some extent, like what is seen in many boils and abscesses, and some of them are cut with a three-angled incision, and some of them are cut from them like the shape of an acacia leaf, or the tumor of the Arab.
And some of them use the circular incision and the crescent-shaped incision, and similar incisions, but if it does not have a head like the smooth, flat tumors, it is necessary to cut with a simple knife only. And if the tumor is large and has collected a lot of fluid and you have cut into it, do not rush to remove all the pus at that time.
But remove some of it and then tighten the tumor for another day, and then remove some more pus also, do this repeatedly on a gradual basis until all of it is removed.
Especially if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man, for often the animal soul separates with the discharge of pus in a lump and perhaps the patient dies while you are unaware. So beware of this chapter with extreme caution.
After striking these tumors, it is necessary to wipe the wound and look. If the tumor's wound is small or the incision was a simple one, use lint made of cotton or flax. But if the tumor is large and the incisions from striking are many...
...then you should insert a wick into each incision until some reach each other. If the tumor has had some of its skin cut or hardened, it is necessary to stuff it with clean cotton or linen without moisture and tighten it until the third day.
Then remove it and treat it with the appropriate ointments until it heals. If bleeding occurs during your work, use cold water and vinegar after soaking a linen cloth in them and apply it to the site of bleeding several times.
If the bleeding persists, you should use the arrangements, treatment, and remedies that we have described in many places in this book and the classification. If you are in wintertime and the tumor site is full of nerves, it is necessary to moisten the dressings with hot syrup and oil.
And place them on the site. If you are in summer and the sites are hot, it is necessary to carry the dressings soaked with water and oil or syrup and oil, all cold until the third day as we said, then remove the tumor and wipe it.
And use in its treatment what is similar until it heals. This is what you need to know about the treatment of tumors in general. As for the detailed method, I have mentioned each tumor and how to treat it separately, summarized and explained.
Chapter Forty-one.
In the incision for tumors that appear in the skin of the head.
Tumors, small in size, appear on the skin of the head and are of kinds of growths that contain sacs; these have conditions like a hen's gizzard, and their types are manysome fatty, some containing moisture resembling mud.
And some contain moisture resembling broth and soup, and so forth, and some are hardened and solid; all of these pose no danger in incision and removal, unless a vein is encountered upon cutting into them.
And the work in cutting into them is to first probe them with the instrument whose image comes after this one, called the "probe," until you learn what they contain. If what they contain is moisture, cut it open a lengthwise incision, a simple incision of this form: .
And begin the incision from line ~b~ to line ~j~. And if the moisture empties, then remove the sac that contained that moisture and cut it entirely; leave nothing of it whatsoever, for often it returns if anything remains.
Then, dip cotton in the ointment of "sorcery" if it is present; otherwise, in salt water, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day, for it consumes what remains of the sac. Then, repeat the application of the cotton with the "sorcery" a second and third time if need be.
Until you are certain that nothing remains of the sac, then treat the wound with ointments until it heals. If the tumor contains a fatty growth, cut it open in this form: .
A crosswise incision and place the knife blades at the edges of the wound, and remove it from each side, and exert your effort in removing the sac that contains it. And if a vein is encountered, do what I have described before; and likewise do in the tumor if it is hardened upon cutting.
And the treatment with a single incision, as mentioned, and the incision on the hardened tumor is easier because it has little blood and moisture, and some of these tumors in the head of some people have no moisture at all, for when I incised a tumor...
...the head of an elderly woman, I found the tumor like solid rock, coarse white, which could not be broken even if someone threw it, and none of the other tumors that occur in the head were like this except for those that occur in the heads of children.
And at the origins of the ears, cut them all with a simple incision and make their bottom from their lowest points so that it is easy for the matter to flow downwards, then treat them with what suits them from treatment.
Chapter Forty-Two.
In the incision on tumors that appear in the neck, these tumors often appear in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin, and they may appear in all parts of the body.  The one that appears in the neck from it may be one, and it may be many, and some are generated from each other.
And every tumor from them is within a special peritoneum, as in the masses and tumors of the head as we described. And the types of these tumors are many, some hardened, some containing moisture, and some malignant that do not respond to treatment.
So I did not see any of them in good condition to the touch, and its appearance was close to the color of the skin, it moved in every direction, and it was not attached to a nerve in the neck or tendon or artery, nor was it sunken. So it is necessary to cut it with a simple incision from above to the bottom of the body in this shape from line ~a~ to line ~b~:
And peel it from every side and extend the edges of the skin with a suture or two sutures or many sutures if needed, as we said in tumors of the head, and remove it gradually little by little, so that it does not cut a vein or nerve, and let the scalpel be not too sharp.
Lest your hand increase the severing or agitate the sick one, cut what you do not need to cut; if you have severed an artery or vein and it has made your hand useless, put in the wound powdered alum or some fragments that stop the blood.
Close the wound and leave it until the inflammation subsides and the wound relaxes and begins to heal; for when the blood stops then return to your work until you are finished, then examine with your index finger if any remaining small clots remain, cut them and clean them.
If in the root of the clot there is a large artery, it is necessary that you do not cut that clot from its root but bind it with a double strong thread and leave it until it falls of itself without harm; then fill the wound with clean cotton which has been soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it.
And if you have cut the clot entirely, it is necessary that you bring together the edges of the wound and sew it from an hour after you have ascertained that there remains no shred; if you see that there remains a shred because of the size of the clot.
It is necessary that you aim for the root and base when cutting it, and use stitching as we have mentioned; and whatever of the clots contains moisture, cover it with a simple pad where you see the place of ripening, and make the pad as below as we have said.
Then use after the pad, the ointment as Egyptian ointment and its likes so that it eats what remains of the corruption until if you see that the wound has healed, treat it with ointments for promoting flesh until it heals.
Chapter Thirty-Four.
In the incision of the larynx about a swelling that occurs inside the throat.
The ancients mentioned this incision in the larynx, and I have not seen anyone in our country perform it; this is the order of their words; as for those who suffer from angina, it is necessary that they avoid the incision in the larynx because they do not benefit from it.
For the purpose of all wounds and lungs to be sound, as for those who have a hot tumor in the mouth or throat or tonsils if there is no cause in the trachea, it is necessary to use a tracheotomy to escape from the damage that comes from suffocation.
When we want to do this, it is necessary to make an incision in the larynx under three circles of the trachea or four small incisions across between two circles as much as the incision in the peritoneum and not in the cartilage, this place is suitable for the incision.
Because it is devoid of flesh and blood vessels are far from it, if the operator is cowardly, it is necessary to extend the skin of the throat with a suture and then cut the skin until when he reaches the trachea beside blood vessels if he sees anything of them.
Then he cuts the peritoneum that we described, and relies on the incision of the trachea from the phlegm that comes out of it with what is crushed and from the interruption of the voice and leaves the wound open for a time, and if the time during which he was afraid of suffocation has passed, gather the edges of the wound from the skin.
And its path alone without the cartilage, then medicinal drugs are used that grow flesh until it heals, said the author of this book, explanation of this passage which we have narrated is if they see the patient has blocked his throat with one of these tumors mentioned.
And the patient, in dire straits on the brink of death, and worried that he would suffocate, they went to tracheotomy so that the patient could breathe at the wound site some air and escape from death, but they ordered the wound to be left open until the end of the disease's verse and its verse for three days or so.
Then, they ordered the wound to be sewn and treated until it healed. And what I saw with my own eyes, a servant took a knife and sent it on her throat, cutting some of her trachea. She was summoned for treatment, and she was found to be rotting like a slaughtered animal, so the wound was revealed.
I found that the blood coming out of the wound was flowing easily, so I knew that she had not severed an artery or vein. Air was coming out of the wound, so I inserted a probe and made a cut in the wound and treated it until he recovered, and nothing else happened to him except for a little noise in his voice, no more.
And after some days she returned to her best condition, so from here we say that a cut in the larynx is not dangerous.
Chapter forty-four.
In the incision on the tumor that appears in the pharynx from outside and is called a pharyngeal vesicle.
This tumor that is called a pharyngeal vesicle is a large tumor on the color of the body and it is common in women, and it comes in two types.
Either it is natural, or it is a secondary growth, the natural one there is no cure for, and the secondary ones come in two types: one similar to fatty tumors, and the other similar to the tumor that arises from the complication of an artery, and its incision is dangerous. So it should not be touched with iron at all except if it was small, if you probe it and explore it with the probe, its nature resembles a fatty tumor and it wasn't attached to any blood vessels, so you cut it as you cut into fatty tumors. And remove it with what it contains from the sac if it is in a sac, otherwise, investigate all of it then treat the area with the appropriate treatment.
Chapter forty-five.
In the incision on types of fatty tumors.
Fatty tumors come in many types, and I have mentioned all their types in the classification, and it is necessary for us to explain here the difference between a fatty tumor and an abscess because it is a problem, so I say that an abscess comes with heat, fever, and frightening pains until the boiling of the phlegm subsides. The pus completes and at that time the fever and pain subside, and there is no heat or fever or aches with it, and it contains itself in a peritoneum sac which has a special covering and is on the color of the body and its beginning is like a lentil and it becomes like a gourd and larger and smaller.
And it is of two kinds, either fatty or that it contains moisture and the colors of the moisture are many as I mentioned in the classification, so if you reach to treat the abscess, dry it and examine it first with the instrument called the 'al-mads' as it comes in its image in the chapter after this one.
Measure the size of the swelling, then bring out the 'al-mads' and look at what comes out in its wake. If a fluid exits, whatever its color, make a small incision as mentioned in all other swellings. And if no moisture comes out after the 'al-mads', know that it is fatty.
Make an incision on it, a crosswise one like I have taught you, and suspend it with the skewers and remove the skin from every side gently and be careful with the sac if you can extract it whole with the abscess.
If the sac ruptures during the work and you were unable to extract it whole, this happens often, then extract it piece by piece until nothing remains of it, because if something remains of it, whether little or much, the abscess will return on most occasions.
If you are overwhelmed and some remains, then widen the wound when you finish with some sharp pointed instruments and suture the wound and put on top of it what calms the hot swelling and treat it with all other treatment until it heals. And if the abscess is large, outline its edge and treat it with what promotes healing.
If a running or non-running vein crosses you and bleeding appears, act quickly, widen the area with powdered alum and leave it tightened for two or three days until the wound becomes septic and the boiling of blood subsides then return to cutting what remains of the abscess.
Chapter Sixty-Four.
On the Images of Instruments.
Of which instruments there are three kinds: large, medium, and small.
Image of a Large Probe:.

The Twenty-Fifth Chapter
On the Treatment of the Fistula
A fistula is caused by many reasons, either from a tear in the peritoneum on the abdomen that brings out the intestines or bowels as it appears in other fistulas, or from blood emanating from a vein or artery as previously mentioned, or from air trapped within.
And if it is from a tear in the peritoneum and protrusion of the intestines, then its color is similar to the color of the body, and it is soft without pain and appears different positions And if it was before the intestines emerged, then its placement with what we described would be more different. If you press it with your fingers, it disappears then returns and perhaps there is a crackling sound with it and it becomes much larger upon entering the bath and severe exertion. If it was before moisture, then it would be soft.
It does not disappear if you press it with your hand nor does it increase or decrease. If it was before blood, then with these signs the tumor appears to blackness. If it was before newly-grown flesh, then the tumor would be hard and solid and remains at a constant amount.
If it was before air, then touching it would be soft. The action in this is that you look and if the navel protrusion is from before blood of the artery or vein or air then it is necessary to refrain from treating it because there is fear and danger as I informed you in the chapter where I mentioned the tumors that occur from before the artery and vein.
If the navel protrusion is from before the intestines or the  spleen, then it is necessary to order the sick person to hold their breath and stand upright stretched out, then learn by the pencil around the entire navel. Then order him to lie down in front of you on his back, then cut around the navel with a wide scalpel at the place which you learned with the pencil, then extend the center of the tumor upwards with a large string and then tie the place of the incision with strong thread or silk thread tightly.
And the knot of the tie should be a loop, then open the center of the stretched tumor above the tie and insert your index finger and ask for the intestines, if you found that the tie took it, loosen the loop and push the intestines back into the abdomen, and if you find a spleen, extend it with a string.
And cut its excess, if an artery or vein obstructs you, tie it properly and return to your work and take two needles, insert two strong threads into them, and insert the two needles into the incision you made around the tumor as staples which you have driven in, then tighten the tumor in four places on the needles.
And if you wish, remove the stitches and leave the site until the flesh drawn tight rots and falls off by itself or cut it when it softens and rots, then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals. If the protruding part of the navel is from flesh growing in it.
Or if it is from moisture, it is necessary to cut the swelling as we have said and bring out the blood or moisture that you find in it, then treat it with what mends the place.
The Third and Fifty-First Chapter.

For I have not been able to cure anyone from it, and before me, I did not see anyone else who reached that, and the work in it if it is feasible as we said, then proceed so that the patient is freed from the black matter repeatedly, then dissect it if it is in the veins with clear fullness.

But squeeze the areas and let all the thick blood flow with your hand or by any means you have available. If a large bleeding occurs in the course of work from cutting an artery or vein, then stop the bleeding until it stops completely, then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.

And cut between the anus and the women not in the middle but to the side of the left thigh, and the incision is on the same stone and your finger in the anus and you press it outwards, making the incision wide from outside and narrow from inside as much as possible to allow the stone to come out.
If it is large, perhaps pressure may be applied with the finger in the seat of the stone when incisions are made so that it comes out without difficulty; and know that there may be stones which have angles and letters, making it difficult for them to come out because of this.
And some are smooth, like the olive, and round, so it is easy for them to come out; and whatever of them has angles and letters, a little more incision should be made; and if it does not come out this way, then it is necessary to maneuver with it, either by grasping it with a clamp that is tight and whose tip is like a scalpel.
So that it may hold onto the stone so that it does not escape, or else a fine instrument with a pointed end can be inserted under it; and if you cannot maneuver it this way, widen the incision a little; if something of blood overpowers you, then cut it off with alum.
And if there are more than one, first push the largest to the mouth of the bladder, then make an incision on it, and then push the smaller ones after that; and do the same if there are more than two; and if it is very large, it is ignorance to make a large incision on it because it exposes the patient to one of two things.
Either that he may die, or that there will always be a dribbling of urine because it does not at all heal together; but try to push it until it comes out, or maneuver in breaking it with forceps until you extract it completely.
And if you have finished your work, wash the wound with vinegar and patience and a soft cloth and tie it up and put over it a piece of cloth moistened with oil and syrup or rose grease and cold water so that the hot swelling subsides; then let the patient lie on his back and do not tighten the bandage until the third day.
And if it dissolves, the place will ooze with water and oil a lot, then treat it with palm ointment and basilica ointment until it heals; and if there is a hot swelling in the wound, an abscess, and so forth, like when blood clots in the bladder and urine becomes obstructed, which is known from the exit of blood with the urine.
Then insert your finger into the wound and bring out that blood for if it remains, it calls for corruption of the bladder and its turning foul, then wash the wound with vinegar and water and salt and treat each kind according to what resembles it from treatment until it heals.
It is necessary during all times of treatment that the thighs be bound and brought together to secure the medicines which are placed on the site, if the stone is small and has become in the urethra and lodged there and urine outflow is prevented then treat it with what I have described before it reaches the fissure.
Therefore often I have dispensed with this treatment by incision, for I have tried it which is that you take a bent piece of steel whose form is:
Triangular tip sharp, inserted in a rod, then take a thread and tie it to the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder then insert the curved iron gently into the urethra until the curve reaches the same stone.
And turn the curve with your hand in the same stone little by little as you strive to pierce it until it passes through from the other side for urine flows out from its hour then close your hand on what remains of the stone from outside the penis and it shatters and comes out with the urine and the ailment heals.
If this treatment does not become prepared for you because of an obstacle that prevents you from it, then tie a thread under the stone and another thread above the stone then make an incision on the stone in the same penis between the two knots and then remove it.
Then the knot is undone and the clotted blood that has become in the wound is cleaned, but it was necessary to tie the thread under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder and the other knot above so that when the thread is untied after the removal of the stone the skin returns to its place and covers the wound.
Therefore, it is necessary for you when tying the upper thread to raise the skin above so that it returns when you are finished and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter Sixty-One.
On Removing Kidney Stones From Women.
Kidney stones are rarely produced in women; however, if one of them suffers from a kidney stone, it is difficult to treat and there are many reasons for this impediment: one is that the woman may be a virgin, and the second is that you will not find a woman who permits herself to the physician.
If she is a chaste woman or belongs to those who are closely related, and the third is that you will not find a woman skilled in this craft, especially working with her hands, and the fourth is that the location of the incision on the kidney stones of women is far from the location of the stone, so it requires a deep incision.
And in this danger, if necessity demands it, it is necessary to take a skilled female physician, and rarely are they found; if she is lacking, then seek a chaste and virtuous male physician or procure a capable midwife skilled in the affairs of women or a woman who points towards this craft somewhat.
So, procure her and command her to do all that you command her regarding the examination of the kidney stone first of all; that is, to see if the woman is a virgin, it is necessary for her to insert her finger into her vulva and examine the kidney stone; if she finds it, she presses it under her finger.
Then, when she has done this, command her to make the incision upon her; if she is not a virgin but rather one who is married, order the midwife to insert her finger into the vulva of the afflicted woman and examine the kidney stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and pressing it firmly.
If she finds it, it is necessary for her to guide it from the opening of the bladder downwards as far as her power allows until it reaches the root of the groin, and then she should make an incision upon her opposite half of the vulva at the root of the groin from whichever direction she feels the kidney stone in that area.
And the finger must not be removed from under the stone, and let the incision be small at first, then the probe is inserted through that small incision, if she feels the stone, increase in the incision as much as you know that the stone will come out of it, and know that there are many kinds of stones.
Some are small and large, smooth and rough, long and oval, and some with branches, so know their types that you may infer what you want. And if blood overcomes you, throw crushed saffron in the place and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops, then return to your work.
Until the stone comes out, and do that you count with yourself from the instruments that were mentioned in extracting the stone for men to help you in your work. And if blood overcomes you and you know by the pulse of blood that it is from a severed artery, place gold dust on the place.
And tighten it with the pliers firmly and leave it, and do not touch it, and leave the stone and do not extract it, for perhaps the ailment will perish, then treat the wound, if the sharpness of the blood subsides after days and the place is cleansed, return to your work until the stone comes out.

The ninth and sixty chapter.
In castration.
Castration in our religion is forbidden.

Such as sheep, oxen, cats, and the like of animals.  I say that castration is done in two ways: either by softening or by cutting. The one done by softening is that we put the animal in hot water until its testicles relax and soften and hang down.
Then you soften it with your hand until it dissolves and is not visible to the touch. As for castration by cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and squeeze its scrotum skin with the left hand, then tie the testicles and make a single incision on each testicle.
Even if the two testicles protrude, cut them after detaching them and leave nothing of the membranes on them except the thin membrane that is on the vessels, and this type of castration is better than the one done by crushing.
Because crushing may leave something from the females, and the animal desires intercourse, then the wound is treated until it heals.

And I make known each shape of it and how the maneuver is in it that you may deduce from it and stand upon it, if the fetus emerges with its head, the natural exit, and intensifies upon the woman and makes her labor difficult, and you see that her strength has weakened, so you seat her on a stool and order women to control her.
And you fill her womb with cooked lentils and wet poultices, then the midwife enters between her fingers a small scalpel and incisions the placenta with it or tears it with her fingernail until what is in it of moisture spills out and she squeezes the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, it is necessary that you inject the woman with licorice saliva mixed with shea butter, then order her after the injection to strain and make her sneeze with a handkerchief and hold her mouth and nose because the fetus will emerge within an hour. If the hand of the fetus emerges first, it is necessary that you return it gently little by little.
If it does not come to enter, place the woman on a platform and raise her legs above then shake the platform on the ground and the woman holds so as not to fall when shaking. If the hands do not enter and the fetus dies, cut them off and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or tie his hands with a rope and pull them moderately because it will come out. The exit of the fetus on its legs, if the fetus emerges on its legs, it is necessary that you push them up then turn the fetus little by little until you smooth it out and then take one of its legs and extend it little by little.
If they came out to the thighs, order that they be washed and lubricated with a kind of ointment, for it will come out. If it does not come out as described, then return the fetus slightly little by little until you make it into its natural shape, for it will then come out smoothly. If it resists all of what has been described.
Take from the saliva of the  catmint, the saliva of the cumin, the fat of sheep's wool and a mixture of wax and pound all together in a mortar with a good pounding, then apply it to the woman's genitals and lower abdomen and then make her sit in lukewarm water until she reaches the navel.
If you see that it has loosened below her, make for her a pad of wool and she should bear it. If she holds the pad for an hour then make her sit on the chair, then lubricate her and close her mouth and nose, and squeeze her lower abdomen gently. The fetus will come out in an hour's time, coming out on its knees and hands.
If it comes out in this manner, hold back the introduction of its hands little by little, then make the woman lie on her back and lower her legs while she is lying down on a bed and she clasps her hands together, then squeeze gently on her abdomen little by little. Then take out what is under her legs from the cushions until she is positioned downwards. If the fetus does not come out, take both of her legs and move them with a strong motion then squeeze gently above the navel until the fetus ascends upwards, then the midwife inserts her hand and smooths out the fetus little by little.
And order the woman to wash herself until the fetus comes out, coming out with one hand extended. Hold back its hand if you are able to return it. If you cannot return it, make the woman stand and walk. If she cannot walk, then lay her down.
She lay down and her leg was shaken violently then the lactuce (instrument) which I have described from the  instruments was used. If she took hold of it, she was seated on a stool and treatment was given to return the hand and set the fetus in its natural form. The woman was made to cough and ordered to strain until it came out.
The fetus comes out on its back, extending its hands and with its face toward the mother's back. It is necessary for the midwife to grasp the child's hand and turn it gradually and gently until it is straightened, then apply the fat and instruments that I have described to the head.
Then order her to move a little, and when she has done so, seat her on the stool and order her to lean to the right side then order her to strain and have her cough with the (instrument) kends for it comes out. The fetus comes out standing on its side.
If it descends to the mouth of the womb in this manner with the placenta, then split the placenta with your fingernail until it is free from moisture. If it clings to the face of the fetus and its neck, cut it from the navel so that it will not suffocate and die, then push the fetus back inside until it is placed as it should be.
And order the woman to strain several times for it comes out easily. As for twins or many fetuses, know that twins often are born, and sometimes three or four, but this is rare. As for five, it is something outside of nature, they do not live at all.
And they are surrounded by one placenta, and they are separated by a partition between them, attached to the navel of each one of them. They may come out as easily as a single fetus, or they may come out in a difficult manner as we have described.
If the delivery of some of them is difficult and it becomes as we have said, in unnatural forms, then treat it as we have described. Let the midwife be gentle and do what she does with care and patience and contrive for every shape what appears to her from the means leading to safety.
Mentioning what is imagined in the womb of fetuses that are expelled, it may be imagined in the womb one and two and three and four and five and six and seven and more than ten. It has been proven to me that a woman miscarried seven and another fifteen, all of them imagined thus.
By the estimation of the wise and knowing, all of this ought to be in the knowledge of the midwife because perhaps something like this will happen to her one day, so she may meet it with what is appropriate,.
The sixth and seventy chapter.
In extracting the dead fetus.
If you treated the dead fetus with what I mentioned in the division of treatment and it did not come out, and forced you to work with your hand, then it is necessary for you to look. If the woman is healthy in strength and there is nothing from the symptoms that one fears harming her, then it is necessary for the woman to lie on a bed on her back.
And her head be tilted downwards and her legs elevated, and a servant controls her from both sides or ties her to the bed so that her body does not be pulled when extracting the fetus.
Then he lubricates the mouth of her womb with moist ointments, along with honey and thyme and flaxseed. Then the midwife smears her hand with these ointments and saliva then she inserts it into the womb gently, then seeks a place for her to insert forceps from the fetus, and the appropriate places for that.
Look, if the fetus is coming down so that it descends on its head, then insert the forceps into its eyes or cheekbone or mouth or under the chin or throat or in the places near the ribs or below the breasts.
And as for if its descent is on its legs, then in the groin and the middle ribs, it is necessary to hold the forceps with the right hand and make its curve between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand gently and insert a forceps into some of those places that we mentioned.
Until you reach an empty space, then insert another or a third probe in front of it if you need the pull to be equal and not lean in one direction, then stretch it out to a level length and do not make the stretching only straight but move it in all directions.
To make it easier to come out as is done with the molar when extracting it, and it is necessary in this process to loosen the tension. If something gets stuck, then it is necessary to lubricate some of the fingers of the midwife with oil and insert them from one side to guide what is stuck. If part of the fetus comes out, then the probes are moved to other positions.
It is slightly raised, doing this until the whole fetus comes out. If a hand comes out before the others and cannot be returned due to its compression, it is necessary to wrap a cloth around it then pull it until it all comes out, then cut it.
As for the wrist or elbow, and so on, it is necessary to do the same with the other hand and feet. If the head of the fetus is large and there is pressure on its exit, or if there is accumulated water in its head, it is necessary to insert a sharp knife between the fingers.
And split it with it, the head comes out of the water or you make a hole in it with the instrument called the "mashakh" whose image comes with the images of all other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
Similarly, do this if the fetus is large-headed by nature, of course, it is necessary to split the skull or smooth it with the mashakh as we said, then extract the bones with tweezers. If the head comes out and compresses at the collarbone, then split it until the moisture in the chest drains.
Because the chest then joins, if the chest does not join and it doesn't come out, cut as much as you can. If the lower abdomen is a tumor or has a boil, it is necessary to crush it until the moisture comes out of it.
If the fetus is on its legs, then pulling it out is easy and straightening it to the mouth of the womb is simple. But if it is compressed in the abdomen or chest, it is necessary to pull it with a rope that you have wrapped around your hand and cut open the abdomen or chest until what is in them flows out.
If all the organs have been removed and the head remains and is held back, let the midwife insert her left hand. If the mouth of the womb is open, she inserts her hand into the neck of the womb and grasps the head with her fingers, pulling it to the mouth of the womb, then she inserts a rope or two ropes and pulls it with them.
If the mouth of the womb has closed due to a hot swelling, it should not be forced. Rather, at that time it is necessary to use applications of wet, fatty things and use compresses and sit in waters that soften and moisten.
As for if the fetus is on its side, if it is possible to straighten it, then use what was mentioned for a living fetus. If it is not possible, then cut it and remove it. It is necessary that nothing of the placenta be left inside at all. When you have finished treatment, use what was mentioned from treatment for hot swellings that appear in the wombs.
If bleeding occurs, then go down into binding waters and use all the treatment. And I have seen a woman who was pregnant, the fetus died in her womb, then she became pregnant with it again.
Then the other fetus also died. After a long time, a swelling appeared in her groin and it swelled until it opened and began to discharge pus. I was called to treat her and treated her for a long time but the wound did not close. So I placed some strong ointments on it.
Then a bone came out from the place, and she continued for some days, and another bone came out. I was amazed by this because the abdomen is not a place for bones. I estimated that it was from the bones of the dead fetus. So I searched the wound and extracted many bones from the skull of the fetus.
And I did not stop until I removed many bones from it and the woman was in the best of health. And she lived for a time, pus coming out from the place slowly, but that is why I bring this rare case here.
Because it contains knowledge and aid to what the physician who creates with his hand tries to do in treatment.
Chapter Seventy-Seven.

And their curvature towards a finger and their length an inch and a half, and in the middle of the two pieces, there are two grooves made from the same kind of wood that have been tightly fastened into them, their length is half an inch or slightly more, and their width is about two fingers or slightly more, and these two grooves.
Are the ones that enter into the mouth of the womb to open it when you operate with the screws, an image of another tool like this gentler and lighter.

So you seat the woman on a reclining bed with her legs spread apart between her thighs, then insert these two grooves pressed together into the mouth of the womb while you hold the end of the tool below between her hip bones, and then open your hand with the tool as you do with a calamus, either to the extent that you want to open the womb.
