You press your back against his face and make his leg between your legs, then you clasp his knee with your hands and interlace them between your fingers on his knee, then you press the sides of his knee with your hands firmly and another servant stretches his leg until the knee returns to its place.
And the sign of its return is that you press the leg to the thigh in a soft, unforced manner, then bandage it and press the leg to the thigh again, then tie them all together with a strip for three or four days, then release them, and he should not use except for little walking for several days until it strengthens.
If returning it as we described proves difficult for you, then use strong traction with the straps that I have previously described in the treatment of the hip until it returns.
Chapter Thirty-Third.
In Treating a Broken Heelbone.
The heel bone may be displaced slightly, or it may completely break, and its fracture is either inward or outward, and the sign of its fracture is that you see the heel swollen and protruding in the direction to which it fractured.
As for the treatment of its displacement, it is easy to return it by gently stretching it and straightening it until it returns. But if it fractures completely, it is necessary that you seat the patient seated and a strong servant grasps him from behind his back in the middle.
Then you grasp his foot from its upper part with your right hand and from below his ankle with your left hand, then pull the foot towards you with your right hand and then with your left twice, then stretch it with your left and push the front of the foot with your right towards the leg without force.
Do this twice as we have described, then push the front of the foot to the leg in the third time while you pull the ankle, if it returns in one or two attempts with this method and you see the foot leveled, otherwise repeat the work on it because it will return.
If it does not return for you by what we have described, then lay the patient on his back on the ground and insert a wedge into the earth firmly so that it falls between his thighs. And you have wrapped a cloth on it so as not to harm the patient, then hold his thigh firm.
Then, another attendant stretches the man's leg either with his hands or with a bandage tied to his neck. Then each attendant stretches in opposition to the stretch of his companion, and the wedge stands between the patient's thighs, holding it so that his body does not sag downwards during the stretching, then the physician sets the jaw with his hands.
And another attendant holds the healthy leg downwards, for the jaw returns quickly. If the jaw returns and you see that its return is correct, then take the dressing and the splint and tighten it with strong bandages, and tie the foot with a bandage to the bottom, and it is necessary to avoid the nerve that is above the heel from behind.
So that the bandage is not tight on it and harms him, then leave him for two or three days. If the bandage relaxes, tighten it again, then release it on the third or fourth day. The patient refrains from walking for forty days.
If he intends to walk before this period, do not be assured that the jaw will not break and spoil, and it will not accept treatment after that. If a hot swelling appears on him, it is necessary to use what we have described elsewhere in the treatment and cauterization until it goes away.
Chapter Forty-Third.
In the Treatment of a Broken Finger.
It is necessary to set what has broken from it with a slight stretching, without violence, and this is not difficult, but it is easy. If the fracture is in some of the bones of the heel, then it is necessary to make the patient's foot on a flat place on the ground.
Or on a board and he is standing like the walking one, then you stand and put your foot on what remained of those joints then stamp it with your foot forcefully until it returns and you see that it has become straight and there does not appear in the place any projection.
Then put under the sole of his foot a board that takes the whole foot, it should have two heads then tighten it tightly and firmly for three days then remove it and protect him from walking for many days until it strengthens and the return is prevented, God willing.
The Fifth Thirty-First Chapter.
In Types of Jaw Fracture Which Is With a Wound or With a Fracture or Both
When something of that happens and it is treated and healed, often death follows.
Therefore it is not fitting to undertake the treatment of such a thing except by one who is skillful in the craft, long experienced, gentle, compassionate, patient, not hasty or reckless and that he should use at the beginning medicines that calm hot swellings only and reassure the sick person.
To the power of God, except what I have hoped for his safety from disease with a light sickness and you have seen in it some hope, so return him to your mercy at first before the hot swelling happens.
If the limb returned to what I have desired, then use the arrangement that calms hot swellings and treat the wound with whatever ointments are suitable for it of drying ones, if the jaw was fractured and there were bone fragments protruding, then remove them. And follow in that what we have mentioned in simple diseases previously in their places.
And take care in your effort and purify yourself from entering the path of speculation as I have previously mentioned and advised you, for that is better for your standing and safer for your exposure, God willing.
